\allowdisplaybreaks

\title[Generalizations of Mirzakhani's recursion and Masur-Veech volumes]
{Some generalizations of Mirzakhani's recursion and Masur-Veech volumes
via topological recursions}



\author[H.\ Fuji]{Hiroyuki Fuji}
\address{H.~Fuji: 
Department of Information and Computer Science\\
Faculty of Information Science and Technology\\
Osaka Institute of Technology\\
Kitayama, Hirakata City, Osaka 573-0196, Japan\\
and 
%\newline
Yukawa Institute for Theoretical Physics, Kyoto University,
Kitashirakawa Oiwakecho, Sakyo-ku, Kyoto 606-8502, Japan
}
\email{hiroyuki.fuji@oit.ac.jp}





\author[M.\ Manabe]{Masahide Manabe}
\address{M.~Manabe:
Osaka Central Advanced Mathematical Institute\\
Osaka Metropolitan University\\
3-3-138 Sugimoto, Sumiyoshi-ku, Osaka, 558-8585\\
Japan\\
and 
Department of Mathematics\\
Graduate School of Science\\
Osaka University\\
Toyonaka, Osaka 560-0043\\
Japan}
\email{masahidemanabe@gmail.com}







\begin{abstract}
The Chekhov-Eynard-Orantin's topological recursion gives a Laplace dual representation of 
the Mirzakhani's recursion for the moduli space of bordered hyperbolic Riemann surfaces.
Via the Andersen-Borot-Orantin's geometric recursion, 
a twist of the topological recursion is proposed, and a recursion for the Masur-Veech polynomials is uncovered.
The purpose of this article is to explore the generalization of the Mirzakhani's recursion based on physical two dimensional gravity models related to the Jackiw-Teitelboim gravity.
For generalized Mirzakhani's recursions involving a Masur-Veech type twist, 
we derive Virasoro constraints and cut-and-join equations, and also show some computations of generalized volumes for the physical two dimensional gravity models.
\end{abstract}



\subjclass[2010]{Primary: 81T45, 14D21, 14N10
Secondary:  	32G15, 81T40, 58D29, 05A15}

\keywords{Topological  recursion;  Weil-Petersson volume; Masur-Veech volume;  quantum Airy structure; Jackiw-Teitelboim gravity}

\maketitle

\section{Introduction}\label{sect:Intro}

A remarkable identity \cite{McShane} concerning the lengths of simple closed geodesics on a once-punctured torus 
with a complete finite-area hyperbolic structure is discovered by McShane in his Ph.D thesis \cite{McShane_PhD}.
After his remarkable discovery, the McShane's identity is generalized to hyperbolic Riemann surfaces of 
higher genus with bordered boundaries in a series of Mirzakhani's papers \cite{Mirz3,Mirz1}.
The generalized identity leads to a striking recursion relation for the Weil-Petersson volumes of moduli spaces of 
bordered Riemann surfaces, referred to as \emph{Mirzakhani's recursion}.

\begin{thm}[Mirzakhani's recursion \cite{Mirz3,Mirz1}]
Let $V_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,\ldots.L_n)$ be 
the Weil-Petersson volume for the moduli space of bordered connected Riemann surfaces of genus $g$
with $n$ ordered boundary components of lengths $L_1,\ldots,L_n$.
The Weil-Petersson volumes for $2g-2+n>0$ obey the Mirzakhani's recursion
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\label{eq:Mirzakhani_rec}
L_1V_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)
&=\frac{1}{2}\int_{\mathbb{R}_+^2} 
D^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,\ell,\ell')\, P^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}(\ell,\ell',L_K)\, 
\ell\ell'd\ell d\ell'
\\
&\quad
+\sum_{m=2}^n\int_{\mathbb{R}_+}
R^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,L_m,\ell)\, V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n-1}(\ell,L_{K\setminus\{m\}})\, \ell d\ell,
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $L_K=\{L_2,\ldots,L_n\}$ and $L_J=\{L_{i_1},\ldots,L_{i_{|J|}}\}$
for $J=\{i_1,\ldots,i_{|J|}\}\subset K=\{2,\ldots,n\}$.
Here $P^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}$ is
\begin{align}
&
P^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}(\ell,\ell',L_K)
=V_{g-1,n+1}^{\mathrm{WP}}(\ell,\ell',L_K)+
\mathop{\sum_{h+h'=g}}
\limits_{J \cup J'=K}^{\mathrm{stable}}
V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{h,1+|J|}(\ell,L_J)\, V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{h',1+|J'|}(\ell',L_{J'}),
\label{eq:P_WP}
\end{align}
where stable in the sum means that $g$ and $n$ obeys $2g-2+n>0$, and
$D^{\mathrm{WP}}$ and $R^{\mathrm{WP}}$ are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
D^{\mathrm{WP}}(x,y,z)&=\int_{0}^{x}H^{\mathrm{WP}}(y+z,x')\, dx',
\\
R^{\mathrm{WP}}(x,y,z)&=\frac{1}{2}\int_{0}^{x}
\left(H^{\mathrm{WP}}(z,x'+y)+H^{\mathrm{WP}}(z,x'-y)\right)dx',
\end{split}
\end{align}
where the recursion kernel $H^{\mathrm{WP}}(x,y)$ is
\begin{align}
H^{\mathrm{WP}}(x,y)=\frac{1}{1+\mathrm{e}^{\frac{x+y}{2}}}+\frac{1}{1+\mathrm{e}^{\frac{x-y}{2}}}.
\label{eq:WP_H_function}
\end{align}
Especially for $(g,n)=(0,3), (1,1)$,\footnote{We employ a different normalization for $V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{1,1}(L_1)$ 
compared to the one used in \cite{Mirz3,Mirz1} by a factor of $2$.}
\begin{align}
&V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{0,3}(L_1,L_2,L_3)=1,
\qquad
L_1V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{1,1}(L_1)=
\frac12 \int_{\mathbb{R}_+}
D^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,\ell,\ell)\, \ell d\ell.
\label{eq:Mcshane}
\end{align}
\end{thm}

\begin{table}[t]
  \caption{\label{tab:spectral_curve}$\mathsf{y}$-coordinate functions of physical 2D gravity models.
  $T_p(z)$ and $U_p(z)$ denote the Chebyshev polynomials of the first and second kind, respectively.}
  \centering
  \begin{tabular}{|ll|}
  \hline
  Bosonic model & $\mathsf{y}$-coordinate function  \\
  \hline
KdV  (Kontsevich's matrix model) &$\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z)=z+\sum_{a\ge 2}\mathsf{u}_a z^a$\\
  Weil-Petersson (JT gravity) & $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)=\frac{1}{2\pi}\sin(2\pi z)$ \\
  Airy (topological gravity) & $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{A}}(z)=z$ \\
  FZZT ($(2,p)$ minimal string) & $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)=\frac{(-1)^{\frac{p-1}{2}}}{2\pi} T_p\biggl(\frac{2\pi}{p}z\biggr)$
  \\
  \hline
  Supersymmetric model & $\mathsf{y}$-coordinate function \\
  \hline
  BGW (BGW matrix model) & $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{BGW}}(z)=\frac{1}{z}+\sum_{a\ge 1}\mathsf{v}_a z^a$ \\
  Super Weil-Petersson (JT supergravity) & $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{SWP}}(z)=\frac{1}{z}\cos(2\pi z)$ \\
  Bessel (analogue of topological gravity) & $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{B}}(z)=\frac{1}{z}$ \\
  Brane ($(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring) & $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z)=\frac{(-1)^{\frac{p-1}{2}}}{z} U_{p-1}\biggl(\frac{2\pi}{p}z\biggr)$
\\
\hline
  \end{tabular}
\end{table}

In \cite{EO2007,Eynard:2007fi},
it is shown that a Laplace transform of the Mirzakhani's recursion for the Weil-Petersson volumes 
obeys the \emph{Chekhov-Eynard-Orantin (CEO) topological recursion} \cite{EO2007}.
The CEO topological recursion is originally found in the asymptotic analysis of correlation functions of Hermitian matrix models \cite{Alexandrov:2003pj,Eynard:2004mh},
and the basic data of the recursion relation is extracted from the algebro-geometric data of a \emph{spectral curve}.
The spectral curve $\mathcal{C}$ consists of basic data $(\Sigma;\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},B)$: a compact Riemann surface $\Sigma$, coordinate functions $(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y})$ on $\Sigma^{\otimes 2}$, and 
a bidifferential $B$ on $\Sigma^{\otimes 2}$. 
In this paper, we focus on the following class of spectral curves with the basic data:
\begin{align}
\label{eq:spectral_curve_data_1}
\Sigma=\IP^1,\quad
\mathsf{x}(z)=\frac{1}{2}z^2,\quad B(z,w)=\frac{dz\otimes dw}{(z-w)^2},
\end{align}
where the remaining $\mathsf{y}$-coordinate function is specified depending on the models. 
In particular, the $\mathsf{y}$-coordinate function for
the Laplace dual of the  Mirzakhani's recursion
is $y^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)$ in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}.
This spectral curve resides in the class of the KdV spectral curve in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve} which involves time variables $\mathsf{u}_a$ and leads to the asymptotic expansion of the tau-function of the KdV hierarchy
given by the Kontsevich's matrix integral \cite{Kontsevich}
via the CEO topological recursion \cite{EO2007}.




In recent years, several fascinating developments and extensions of the CEO topological recursion for the  Weil-Petersson volumes 
has been reported in theoretical physics and geometry.
In theoretical physics, the non-perturbative studies of the \emph{Jackiw-Teitelboim (JT) gravity} 
motivated by gauge/gravity correspondence uncovered a novel aspect of the Weil-Petersson volumes and their recursions.
In the Saad-Shenker-Stanford's work \cite{Saad:2019lba},
the Weil-Petersson volume of the moduli space of hyperbolic bordered Riemann surfaces arises
in the computation of the path integral of the partition function in the JT gravity, 
and the physical interpretation of the JT gravity partition function as a matrix integral is pointed out.

In terms of the JT gravity interpretation, the coordinate function of the spectral curve for the Weil-Petersson volumes can be found from the disk partition function of the $(2,p)$ minimal string theory in the background of \emph{Fateev-Zamolodchikov-Zamolodchikov-Teschner (FZZT) brane} 
\cite{Fateev:2000ik,Teschner:2000md} in the $p\to\infty$ limit \cite{Saad:2019lba}.%
\footnote{
The spectral curve for the $(2,p)$ minimal string is also considered in \cite{BergereEynard09}.}
The $(2,p)$ minimal string theory for $p=1$ is, in particular, equivalent to the topological gravity, which is also known as the Kontsevich-Witten's intersection theory on the moduli space of stable curves.
The coordinate function of the spectral curve
for the topological gravity
is the KdV spectral curve with vanishing all the time variables, referred to as the Airy spectral curve.

The Saad-Shenker-Stanford's analysis is further extended to the JT supergravity by the Stanford-Witten's work \cite{Stanford:2019vob}.
The path integral for the partition function of the JT supergravity is performed over the moduli space of super Riemann surfaces which are constructed as Riemann surfaces equipped with a spin structure \cite{Crane,Felder:2019iqj,LeBrun,Rosly,Witten:2012ga,Penner:2015xla,Ip:2016ojn,Ip:2017msi}. 
In \cite{Stanford:2019vob}, a supersymmetric extension of the Mirzakhani's recursion for hyperbolic (Neveu-Schwarz) bordered super Riemann surfaces is derived, and the spectral curve of the CEO topological recursion for the supersymmeric extension of the Weil-Petersson volumes is unveiled.

\begin{thm}[Stanford-Witten's recursion \cite{Stanford:2019vob,Norbury:2020vyi}]
Let $V_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}(L_1,\ldots.L_n)$ be 
the supersymmetric analogue of the Weil-Petersson volume, referred to as the super Weil-Petersson volume, for the moduli space of bordered connected super Riemann surfaces of genus $g$
with $n$ ordered NS boundary components of lengths $L_1,\ldots,L_n$.%
\footnote{
There are several choices of the orientation- and time-reversal symmetries to define the JT supergravity.
Depending on the choice of these symmetries, the sign and power of $2$ factors must be implemented to find the partition function and the supersymmetric volume $V_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}$.
In this article, we adopt the normalization of $V_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ to agree with $V^{\Theta}_{g,n}$ defined in \cite{Norbury:2020vyi} (see eq.\eqref{sw_volume}).
}
The super Weil-Petersson volumes for $2g-2+n>0$ obey 
the same recursion relation as the Mirzakhani's recursion \eqref{eq:Mirzakhani_rec} with replacements:
\begin{align}
V^{\mathrm{WP}}\to V^{\mathrm{SWP}},\quad
D^{\mathrm{WP}}\to D^{\mathrm{SWP}},\quad
R^{\mathrm{WP}}\to R^{\mathrm{SWP}},
\end{align}
where $D^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ and $D^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
D^{\mathrm{SWP}}(x,y,z)&=H^{\mathrm{SWP}}(y+z,x),
\\ 
R^{\mathrm{SWP}}(x,y,z)&=\frac{1}{2}
\left(H^{\mathrm{WP}}(z,x+y)+H^{\mathrm{WP}}(z,x-y)\right),
\end{split}
\end{align}
and the kernel function $H^{\mathrm{SWP}}(x,y)$ is
\begin{align}
H^{\mathrm{SWP}}(x,y)=\frac{1}{4\pi}\left(
\frac{1}{\cosh\frac{x-y}{4}}-\frac{1}{\cosh\frac{x+y}{4}}
\right).
\label{eq:SWP_H_function}
\end{align}
\end{thm}


The spectral curve \cite{Stanford:2019vob,Norbury:2020vyi} for the super Weil-Petersson volumes is found as a specialization of the BGW spectral curve for the tau-function of the Br\'ezin-Gross-Witten (BGW) model \cite{Brezin:1980rk,Gross:1980he}.
The BGW spectral curve involves time variables $\mathsf{v}_a$, and 
the well-known spectral curve referred to as the Bessel spectral curve \cite{Do:2016odu} is found by taking all the time variables to zero.
By comparison with the above bosonic models in the KdV hierarchy, one can naturally consider a one-parameter family 
of spectral curves, which interpolates the Stanford-Witten's curve for the super Weil-Petersson volumes and the Bessel spectral curve,
a supersymmetric analogue of the spectral curve for the $(2,p)$ minimal string.%
\footnote{
The $\mathsf{y}$-coordinate functions for the bosonic model $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{boson}}$ and the supersymmetric model  $\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{super}}$ are related by
\begin{align}
\mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{super}}=\frac{\partial \mathsf{y}^{\mathrm{boson}}}{\partial \mathsf{x}},
\nonumber
\end{align}
where $\mathsf{x}(z)=z^2/2$ for the physical 2D gravity models in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}.
}
From some physical observations, the basic data of the spectral curve for this supersymmetric analogue are
expected to be found from some brane partition functions of type 0A $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring.


In geometry, the frame work of the Mirzakhani's recursion is generalized 
on basis of the Teichm\"uller theory by the Andersen-Borot-Orantin's work \cite{Andersen_GR}, which is named as the \emph{geometric recursion}.
The basic data of the geometric recursion consists of measurable functions on the Teichm\"uller space of a bordered Riemann surface,
and the McShane-Mirzakhani's identity is represented in the framework of the geometric recursion.
In this article, we call the generalized Mirzakhani's recursion as \emph{Andersen-Borot-Orantin (ABO) topological recursion}, 
which arises from the geometric recursion.
And for the above physical 2D gravity models, the ABO topological recursion is obtained as a Laplace dual of the CEO topological recursion. 


In Mirzakhani's another work \cite{Mirz_MV}, 
the enumerative problem of simple closed geodesics in hyperbolic bordered Riemann surfaces is extended and an elegant combinatorial approach to the computation of the \emph{Masur-Veech volume} of the moduli space of quadratic differentials
on the Riemann surface with marked points is formulated explicitly.
In this approach, 
the combinatorial data of the distribution of simple closed geodesics is described by
stable graphs, and the Masur-Veech volumes are computed by combinations of Weil-Petersson volumes.
In recent years, Mirzakhani's combinatorial approach to compute the Masur-Veech volumes is established further in a series of works by Delecroix, Goujard, Zograf, and Zorich \cite{DGZZ1,DGZZ2,DGZZ3,DGZZ4,DGZZ_latest}. (See also \cite{GM18,CMSZBGL} for the related works.)
The Masur-Veech volume $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ for the moduli space of quadratic differentials $q\in \mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ 
is labeled by the order of zeros and poles of $q$.

In particular for the \emph{principal stratum} of the moduli space $\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ of quadratic differentials,
a novel connection between the Delecroix-Goujard-Zograf-Zorich's result \cite{DGZZ_latest} and the ABO topological recursion is proposed in \cite{Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV}.
The ABO topological recursion to compute the Masur-Veech volumes is the Laplace dual of the CEO topological recursion
for the Airy spectral curve accompanied with an action of \emph{twist}. 
The twist action shifts 
the basic data of the ABO topological recursion (i.e. functions $D$ and $R$ in the Mirzakhani's recursion), which implements the combinatorial data of the stable graphs.
It is shown in \cite{Andersen_MV} that
the constant term in the polynomial obtained from the twisted ABO topological recursion for the Airy spectral curve provides the Masur-Veech volume $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$.


In this article, we discuss the following points on basis of the above developments for the physical 2D gravity models listed in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Derivation of the Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion as the Laplace dual of the CEO topological recursion;
\item Direct proof of the twisted CEO topological recursion;
\item Derivation of Virasoro constraints with or without Masur-Veech type twist and their solutions via cut-and-join equations;
\item Physical derivations of the basic data of the spectral curves and the Masur-Veech twist action of the ABO topological recursion.
\end{enumerate}

On the first point, we will obtain the kernel functions of the Mirzakhani's recursion relation for each 2D gravity model 
in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}.
The recursion kernel for each model is listed in Table \ref{tab:kernel}.
\begin{table}[t]
  \caption{\label{tab:kernel} Recursion kernels of physical 2D gravity models. ($\theta$ denotes the Heaviside step function.)}
  \centering
  \begin{tabular}{|ll|}
  \hline
  Bosonic model & Recursion kernel $H(x,y)$ \\
  \hline
   Weil Petersson (JT gravity) & $H^{\mathrm{WP}}(x,y)=\frac{1}{1+\mathrm{e}^{\frac{x+y}{2}}}+\frac{1}{1+\mathrm{e}^{\frac{x-y}{2}}}$ \\
  Airy (topological gravity) & $H^{\mathrm{A}}(x,y)=\theta(y-x)+\theta(-x-y)$ \\
 FZZT ($(2,p)$ minimal string) & $u_j:=\frac{p}{2\pi}\sin\left(j\pi/p\right)$\\
  \multicolumn{2}{|l|}{
  \hspace{1cm}$H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,y)=-\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}(-1)^j\cos\left(\frac{\pi}{p}j\right)
\left(\mathrm{e}^{-u_j(x+y)}\, \theta(x+y)
+\mathrm{e}^{-u_j(x-y)}\, \theta(x-y)\right)
$}\\
\multicolumn{2}{|l|}{$
\hspace{3.45cm}+\sum_{j=0}^{(p-1)/2}(-1)^j\cos\left(\frac{\pi}{p}j\right)
\left(\mathrm{e}^{u_j(x+y)}\, \theta(-x-y)
+\mathrm{e}^{u_j(x-y)}\, \theta(y-x)\right)$}\\
  \hline
  Supersymmetric model & Recursion kernel $H(x,y)$ \\
  \hline
  Super Weil-Petersson (JT supergravity) & $H^{\mathrm{SWP}}(x,y)=\frac{1}{4\pi}\left(
\frac{1}{\cosh\frac{x-y}{4}}-\frac{1}{\cosh\frac{x+y}{4}}
\right)$ \\
  Bessel (topological gravity) & $H^{\mathrm{B}}(x,y)=\delta(x-y)-\delta(x+y)$ \\ 
  Brane ($(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring)& $u'_j:=\frac{p}{2\pi}\sin\left((j-1/2)\pi/p\right)$\\
  \multicolumn{2}{|l|}{
  \hspace{1cm}$H^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(x,y)=\frac{1}{2\pi}\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}(-1)^j
\cos^2\left(\frac{\pi}{p}\left(j-\frac{1}{2}\right)\right)$}\\
\multicolumn{2}{|l|}{
$\hspace{5.4cm}\times \Bigl(\mathrm{e}^{-u'_j(x+y)}\, \theta(x+y)
-\mathrm{e}^{-u'_j(x-y)}\, \theta(x-y)
$}\\
 \multicolumn{2}{|l|}{\hspace{5.5cm}
$+\mathrm{e}^{u'_j(x+y)}\, \theta(-x-y)
-\mathrm{e}^{u'_j(x-y)}\, \theta(y-x)\Bigr)$}\\
\multicolumn{2}{|l|}{$
\hspace{3.5cm}
+\delta_{p,1}\left(\delta(x-y)-\delta(x+y)\right)$}
\\
\hline
  \end{tabular}
\end{table}

On the second point, we will discuss the twisted volume polynomial $V_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ with Masur-Veech type twist $\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}$ for the 2D gravity models listed in Table \ref{tab:kernel}.
For these physical models, the twisted Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion is
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\label{eq:Twisted_rec}
L_1V_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,\ldots,L_n)
&=\frac{1}{2}\int_{\mathbb{R}_+^2}
D[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,\ell,\ell')\, P_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](\ell,\ell',L_K)\, 
\ell\ell' d\ell d\ell'
\\
&\quad
+\sum_{m=2}^n\int_{\mathbb{R}_+} R[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,L_m,\ell)\, V_{g,n-1}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](\ell,L_{K\setminus\{m\}})\, 
\ell d\ell,
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $P_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ is given by eq.\eqref{eq:P_WP} for the twisted volume polynomials, and $D[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ and $R[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\label{eq:twisted_DR}
D[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,L_2,L_3)&=
D(L_1,L_2,L_3)+R(L_1,L_2,L_3)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(L_2)
\\
&\quad
+R(L_1,L_3,L_2)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(L_3)
+L_1\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(L_2)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(L_3),
\\
R[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,L_2,L_3)&=
R(L_1,L_2,L_3)+L_1\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(L_3).
\end{split}
\end{align}
Here the Masur-Veech type twist function $\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}$ is
\begin{align}
\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(\ell)=\frac{1}{\mathrm{e}^{\ell}-1}.
\label{eq:twist_MV}
\end{align}
In fact, the Masur-Veech volume $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ for the moduli space of quadratic differentials on a Riemann surface of genus $g$ with $n$ marked points is the constant term of the twisted volume $V^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ for the symplectic volume $V^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}$ of the moduli space $\mathcal{M}_{g,n}$ of stable curves of genus $g$ with $n$ marked points in the Kontsevich-Witten's theory. 
In this article, we refer to the twist action of the topological recursion by the function $\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}$
as the \emph{Masur-Veech type twist}.

The main claim of this part is the derivation of the CEO topological recursion for the twisted multidifferentials $\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ 
as a Laplace dual of the twisted volumes $V_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$.

\begin{thm}[Twisted CEO topological recursion \cite{Andersen_MV}]
Let $V_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ be the volume polynomial for the physical 2D gravity model listed in Table \ref{tab:kernel}, which has the expansion 
\begin{align}
V_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,\ldots.L_n)=\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n\ge 0}F^{(g)}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\prod_{i=1}^n\frac{L_i^{2a_i}}{(2a_i+1)!}.
\end{align}
The multidifferentials $\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ obtained from $V_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$,
\begin{align}
\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)=
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n\ge 0}F^{(g)}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
\otimes_{i=1}^n\frac{dz_i}{z_i^{2a_i+2}},\quad (2g-2+n>0),
\end{align}
obey the CEO topological recursion twisted by $\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}$ such that
\begin{align}
&\label{eq:CEO_2d}
\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)
=\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}K[\sfm](z_1,w)\, 
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}(w,z_K),
\end{align}
where $z_K=\{z_2, \ldots, z_n\}$,
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
K[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](z,w)
=\frac{(-1)\, dz}{\left(\mathsf{y}(w)-\mathsf{y}(-w)\right)dw}
\left(
\frac{1}{z^2-w^2}+\frac{1}{2}\sum_{\mathfrak{m}\in\mathbb{Z}^*}
\frac{1}{(z+\mfm)^2-w^2}
\right),
\\
&
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}(w,z_K)=\omega_{g-1,n+1}(w,\overline{w},z_K)
+\mathop{\sum_{h+h'=g}}
\limits_{J \cup J'=K}^{\mathrm{no\, (0,1)}}
\omega_{h,1+|J|}(w, z_J)\, \omega_{h',1+|J'|}(\overline{w}, z_{J'}),
\end{split}
\end{align}
and
\begin{align}
\label{eq:bi-differential_twisted}
\omega_{0,2}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](z_1,z_2)
=B[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](z_1,z_2)=\frac{dz_1\otimes dz_2}{(z_1-z_2)^2}+\frac{1}{2}\sum_{\mathfrak{m}\in\mathbb{Z}^*}\frac{dz_1\otimes dz_2}{(z_1-z_2+\mathfrak{m})^2}.
\end{align}
\end{thm}


On the third point, we will discuss an algebraic aspect, 
which is formulated as the \emph{quantum Airy structure} 
\cite{Kontsevich:2017vdc,Andersen:2017vyk}, 
of the ABO topological recursion and the CEO topological recursion. 
For the physical 2D gravity models, we see that the quantum Airy structures 
are equivalent to the Virasoro constraints, where the quantum Airy structures admit the Masur-Veech type twist by a group action in \cite{Andersen:2017vyk} 
and then the Virasoro constraints are twisted as well.
We explicitly obtain solutions of the Virasoro constraints with or without 
Masur-Veech type twist by using the cut-and-join equations in \cite{Alexandrov:2010bn,Alexandrov:2016kjl}, which are derived from the Virasoro constraints, and the group action mentioned above.


On the fourth point, we will discuss a physical interpretation of the Masur-Veech type twist of the ABO topological recursion 
 in terms of the JT gravity.
Via the path integral computations, the bidifferential $B$ in the basic data \eqref{eq:spectral_curve_data_1} of the spectral curve $\cC$ for 
the Weil-Petersson volumes is found from the JT gravity partition function 
on a hyperbolic double trumpet \cite{Saad:2019lba}.
As mentioned above, the basic data $(\IP^1;\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},B[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}])$ of the spectral curve for the twisted CEO topological recursion differs from $\mathcal{C}$ only by a shift of the bidifferential.
In this article, we find that such a shift of the bidifferential is obtained from the partition function of 
a scalar field coupled to the JT gravity fields \cite{Jafferis:2022wez}.

We also discuss the derivation of the basic data of the spectral curve from the partition function for the other physical 2D gravity models 
in the parallel way as the JT gravity.
And it is natural to consider the analogue of the Masur-Veech volume for these models in Table \ref{tab:kernel}.
In this article, we will compute the analogue of the Masur-Veech volume for each 2D gravity model
by the combinatorial method developed in \cite{Mirz_MV,DGZZ_latest} and the twisted CEO topological recursion \eqref{eq:CEO_2d}.


This paper is organized as follows.
In Section \ref{sec:geometric_recursion}
we summarize the formulation of the ABO topological recursion and discuss physical 2D gravity examples.
In Section \ref{sect:MasurVeech}
we show
the combinatorial computation of the Masur-Veech volume $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ 
and its generalization to physical 2D gravity models.
In Section \ref{sec:topological_recursion}
we discuss the CEO topological recursion for physical 2D gravity models, and
derive the twisted CEO topological recursion for generalized Masur-Veech polynomials
as a Laplace transform of the twisted ABO topological recursion.
In Section \ref{sec:virasoro_constraint}
we derive the manifest form of Virasoro generators from the (twisted) ABO topological recursion on basis of the quantum Airy structure, 
and compute free energies by solving cut-and-join equations iteratively for physical 2D gravity models.
In Appendix \ref{sec:physical}
we give a physical interpretation of the Masur-Veech type twist
of the topological recursions by an extra scalar field coupled to the JT gravity fields,
and discuss the derivations of the basic data of the spectral curves for 2D physical models.
%In particular for this section, we discuss in the style of the theoretical physics.
In Appendix \ref{sec:Derivation_Mirz}
we derive the functions $D$ and $R$ in the Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursions for 
the FZZT brane in the $(2,p)$ minimal string and its supersymmetric analogue
from the CEO topological recursion in the similar way as the paper \cite{Eynard:2007fi}.
In Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol}
we give tables of the (twisted) volume polynomials for physical 2D gravity models.

\section{ABO topological recursion}\label{sec:geometric_recursion}

In this section, after recalling the ABO topological recursion \cite{Andersen_GR} which generalizes the Mirzakhani's recursion \cite{Mirz3,Mirz1}, we apply it to the physical 2D gravity models listed in Table \ref{tab:kernel}. In particular, we provide the kernel functions \eqref{eq:H_minimal} and \eqref{eq:H_super_minimal} for the $(2,p)$ minimal string and the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring. 
In Sections \ref{sec:twisting_gr} and \ref{sec:examples_gr_tw}, we also recall the ABO topological recursion with a twist proposed in \cite{Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV}, which generalizes 
the combinatorial formula of the Masur-Veech volume in 
\cite{Mirz_MV,DGZZ_latest} (see Section \ref{sect:MasurVeech}), 
and apply it to the physical 2D gravity models.


\subsection{Formulation}\label{sec:def_gr}

The ABO topological recursion is a framework of recursions for \emph{volume polynomials} defined on the moduli space of connected bordered Riemann surfaces, which is a generalization of the Mirzakhani's recursion.


\begin{Def}[ABO topological recursion \cite{Andersen_GR}]\label{def:geom_rec}
Let $\VO_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ be a volume polynomial
labeled by $g \ge 0, n \ge 1$ satisfying $2g-2+n > 0$, 
on the moduli space $\cM_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ of connected bordered Riemann surfaces of genus $g$ with $n$ ordered boundary components of lengths $L_1, \ldots, L_n$, 
which obeys the ABO topological recursion such that%
\footnote{
In \cite{Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV}, the volume polynomial $\VO_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ is denoted as 
$V\Omega_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$.}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\VO_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\sum_{m=2}^n \int_{\IR_+} \sfB(L_1,L_m,\ell)\, 
\VO_{g,n-1}(\ell, L_{K\setminus \{m\}})\, \ell d\ell
\\
&\qquad
+ \frac12 \int_{\IR_+^2} \sfC(L_1, \ell, \ell')\, 
P_{g,n}(\ell, \ell', L_K)\,
\ell\ell'd\ell d\ell',
\label{geom_rec}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $\IR_+ = [0, \infty)$, $K=\{2,\ldots,n\}$. 
The topological recursion requires our initial data $\sfB(L_1,L_2,\ell)$, $\sfC(L_1, \ell, \ell')$, and 
\begin{align}
\VO_{0,3}(L_1,L_2,L_3)=\sfA(L_1,L_2,L_3),\quad
\VO_{1,1}(L_1)=V\sfD(L_1)
=\int_{\cM_{1,1}(L_1)} \sfD(\sigma)\, d\mu_{\mathrm{WP}}(\sigma),
\label{geom_rec_ini}
\end{align}
where $\mu_{\mathrm{WP}}(\sigma)$ denotes the Weil-Petersson measure on the moduli space
$\cM_{1,1}(L_1)$ endowed with a hyperbolic metric $\sigma$ on a torus with one boundary, and $\sfD(\sigma)$ is a measurable function on $\cM_{1,1}(L_1)$.
Here 
\begin{align}
P_{g,n}(\ell, \ell', L_K)=
\VO_{g-1, n+1}(\ell, \ell', L_K)
+ \mathop{\sum_{h+h'=g}}
\limits_{J \cup J'=K}^{\mathrm{stable}}
\VO_{h, 1+|J|}(\ell, L_J)\, \VO_{h', 1+|J'|}(\ell', L_{J'}),
\label{geo_rec_p}
\end{align}
where $\mathrm{stable}$ in the sum means that $g$ and $n$ obeys $2g-2+n>0$, i.e. $(g,n)=(0,1),\, (0,2)$ are excluded, and 
$L_J=\{L_{i_1}, \ldots, L_{i_{|J|}}\}$, 
$L_{J'}=\{L_{i_{|J|+1}}, \ldots, L_{i_{n-1}}\}$ for 
$J=\{i_1, \ldots, i_{|J|}\} \subseteq K$.
\end{Def}

Assume the expansion of the volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}$ such that
\begin{align}
\VO_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n \ge 0} F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\, 
\prod_{i=1}^n e_{a_i}(L_i),
\label{gr_exp}
\end{align}
where $F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ is referred to as the \emph{volume coefficient} and 
\begin{align}
e_{a}(L)=\frac{L^{2a}}{(2a+1)!}.
\label{e_base}
\end{align}
By
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\int_{\IR_+} \sfB(L_1,L_2,\ell)\, e_{a}(\ell)\, \ell d\ell
=\sum_{a_1, a_2 \ge 0} \sfB^{a_1}_{a_2, a}\, e_{a_1}(L_1)\, e_{a_2}(L_2),
\\
&
\int_{\IR_+^2} \sfC(L_1,\ell,\ell')\, e_{a}(\ell)\, e_{b}(\ell')\, 
\ell \ell' d\ell d\ell'
=\sum_{a_1 \ge 0} \sfC^{a_1}_{a, b}\, e_{a_1}(L_1),
\label{gr_coeff_bc}
\end{split}
\end{align}
the ABO topological recursion \eqref{geom_rec} gives
a recursion for $F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}&=
\sum_{m=2}^n \sum_{b \ge 0} \sfB^{a_1}_{a_m, b}\, 
F^{(g)}_{b, a_2, \ldots, \widehat{a}_m, \ldots,a_n}
\\
&\quad
+\frac12 \sum_{a,b\ge 0} \sfC^{a_1}_{a, b}
\Bigg(F^{(g-1)}_{a,b, a_2, \ldots, a_n} +
\mathop{\sum_{h+h'=g}}
\limits_{J \cup J'=K}^{\mathrm{stable}}
F^{(h)}_{a,a_J}\, F^{(h')}_{b,a_{J'}} \Bigg),
\label{geom_rec_coeff}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $a_J=\{a_{i_1},\ldots,a_{i_{|J|}}\}$ and $a_{J'}=\{a_{i_{|J|+1}},\ldots,a_{i_{n-1}}\}$ for $J=\{i_1,\ldots,i_{|J|}\} \subseteq K$. The initial inputs are $\sfB^{a_1}_{a_2, a}, \sfC^{a_1}_{a, b}$, and
\begin{align}
F^{(0)}_{a_1,a_2,a_3}=\sfA^{a_1}_{a_2, a_3},\qquad
F^{(1)}_{a_1}=\sfD^{a_1},
\label{geom_rec_coeff_ini}
\end{align}
where note that $\sfB^{a}_{b, c}=\sfB^{a}_{c, b}$, $\sfC^{a}_{b, c}=\sfC^{a}_{c, b}$ and $\sfA^{a}_{b, c}=\sfA^{a}_{c, b}=\sfA^{b}_{a, c}$.



\begin{rem}[Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion]\label{rem:mir_rec}
The ABO topological recursion \eqref{geom_rec} is a generalization of 
the Mirzakhani's recursion \cite{Mirz3,Mirz1} for the Weil-Petersson volume 
$V_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ of the moduli space 
$\cM_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ of genus $g$ hyperbolic surfaces with $n$ geodesic boundaries of length $L_1, \ldots, L_n$.
In this article, we call the following form of the ABO topological recursion 
the \emph{Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion}:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
L_1V_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\sum_{m=2}^n \int_{\IR_+}
x R(L_1,L_m,x)\, V_{g,n-1}(x,L_{K \setminus\{m\}})\, dx
\\
&\qquad
+\frac{1}{2}\int_{\IR_+^2}
xy D(L_1,x,y)\, P_{g,n}(x,y,L_K)\, dxdy,
\label{eq:Mirzakhani's}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where
\begin{align}
R(x,y,z)=x\, \sfB(x,y,z),
\qquad
D(x,y,z)=x\, \sfC(x, y, z).
\label{mirz_abo_data}
\end{align}
\end{rem}



\subsection{Bosonic models}\label{sec:examples_gr}

We refer to a class of physical 2D gravity models such as the JT gravity, the topological gravity, 
and the $(2,p)$ minimal string (denoted by resp. WP, A, and M$(p)$) as \emph{bosonic models} (see Table \ref{tab:kernel} in Section \ref{sect:Intro}, and Appendix \ref{sec:physical} for physical arguments).
For the JT gravity, the Weil-Petersson volumes appear in a part of the path integral of the partition function \cite{Saad:2019lba}.
In the Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion \eqref{eq:Mirzakhani's} 
for the bosonic models, two functions $R(x,y,z)$ and $D(x,y,z)$ 
are given in terms of a kernel function $H(x,y)$ as
\begin{align}
R(x,y,z)=\frac{1}{2}\int_0^{x}\left(H(z,t+y)+H(z,t-y)\right)dt,
\quad
D(x,y,z)=\int_0^x H(y+z,t)\, dt.
\label{eq:DR_H_bosonic}
\end{align}
In the following, we will provide the kernel functions $H(x,y)$ for the bosonic models, and find their topological recursions for the volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}$.



\subsubsection{Weil-Petersson volumes}\label{subsec:gr_mir}

The initial data of the ABO topological recursion \cite{Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV} for the Weil-Petersson volumes of moduli spaces of connected bordered Riemann surfaces are 
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\sfA^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,L_2,L_3)&=1,
\\
\sfB^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,L_2,\ell)&=
1 - \frac{1}{L_1}\log 
\left(
\frac{\cosh\bigl(\frac{L_2}{2}\bigr)+\cosh\bigl(\frac{L_1+\ell}{2}\bigr)}
{\cosh\bigl(\frac{L_2}{2}\bigr)+\cosh\bigl(\frac{L_1-\ell}{2}\bigr)}
\right),
\\
\sfC^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1, \ell, \ell')&=\frac{2}{L_1} \log
\left(
\frac{\e^{\frac{L_1}{2}}+\e^{\frac{\ell + \ell'}{2}}}
{\e^{-\frac{L_1}{2}}+\e^{\frac{\ell + \ell'}{2}}}
\right),
\\
V\sfD^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1)&=\frac{\pi^2}{12} + \frac{1}{48}L_1^2.
\label{gr_mir_abcd}
\end{split}
\end{align}
Here the initial data $\sfB^{\mathrm{WP}}$ and $\sfC^{\mathrm{WP}}$ are given 
by the formulae \eqref{mirz_abo_data} and \eqref{eq:DR_H_bosonic} 
with the kernel function
\begin{align}
H^{\mathrm{WP}}(x,y)=
\frac{1}{1+\mathrm{e}^{\frac{x-y}{2}}}+\frac{1}{1+\mathrm{e}^{\frac{x+y}{2}}}.
\label{eq:H_WP}
\end{align}


For this model, the volume polynomial $\VO_{g,n}$ provides 
the Weil-Petersson volume of the moduli space $\cM_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ of 
connected bordered Riemann surfaces \cite{Mirz1}:
\begin{align}
\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\int_{\cM_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)} \exp{\omega^{\mathrm{WP}}}=
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\exp\left(2\pi^2 \kappa_1 + \sum_{i=1}^n \frac{L_i^2}{2}\psi_i\right).
\label{mir_volume}
\end{align}
Here $\omega^{\mathrm{WP}}$ denotes the Weil-Petersson symplectic form, and 
in the last equality, $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}$ is represented by 
the integral of the $\psi$ and $\kappa_1$ classes on 
the moduli space $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$, 
which is the Deligne-Mumford compactification of the moduli space of stable curves of genus $g$ with $n$ marked points.
(This equality is proved in the Wolpert's work \cite{Wolpert}.)
The psi class $\psi_i$ is the first Chern class of the line bundle over 
$\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ with the fiber over the $i$th marked point. 
The first Miller-Morita-Mumford class $\kappa_1$ is a tautological class defined by considering a forgetful map
$\pi: \overline{\cM}_{g,n+1} \to \overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ for 
$\psi^2_{n+1}$. 
By comparison of eq.\eqref{gr_exp} with eq.\eqref{mir_volume}, the Weil-Petersson volume coefficients are found as 
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{WP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
=
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right) 
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\e^{2\pi^2 \kappa_1}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n},
\label{feg_mir}
\end{align}
The volume coefficient $F^{\mathrm{WP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ does not vanish, if the condition below is satisfied:
\begin{align}
\sum_{i=1}^n a_i \le 3g-3+n.
\label{hom_mir}
\end{align}
Some explicit results of $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}$ are listed in 
Table \ref{lst_wp} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_no_twist}.


\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_kappa}
One can introduce a deformation parameter $s$ for the Weil-Petersson volume \eqref{mir_volume} which changes $\kappa_1\to s\kappa_1$, by the replacement $\pi^2 \to \pi^2 s$ in the coefficient $F^{\mathrm{WP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$.
\end{rem}


\subsubsection{Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes}\label{subsec:gr_kw}

In Witten's work \cite{Witten:1990hr},
a novel approach to the intersection theory of the moduli space $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ of stable curves 
is proposed based on the two dimensional topological gravity, and it is conjectured that
the generating function of the Hodge integrals over $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ is given by  
the tau function of the KdV hierarchy. The Witten's conjecture is proved elegantly by Kontsevich's work \cite{Kontsevich}, and the cell decomposition of  $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ on basis of the Strebel's quadratic differential is realized by the metric ribbon graphs \cite{MP98} in his proof.
On basis of the Kontsevich's work, the symplectic volume of the moduli space of stable curves is defined on the space of the metric ribbon graphs in \cite{BCSW}, and is referred to as the \emph{Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volume}.


The initial data of the ABO topological recursion \cite{BCSW,Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV} for the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic
volumes of moduli spaces of stable curves are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\sfA^{\mathrm{A}}(L_1,L_2,L_3)&=1,
\\
\sfB^{\mathrm{A}}(L_1,L_2,\ell)&=
\frac{1}{2L_1}\left(
\left[L_1-L_2-\ell\right]_+ - \left[-L_1+L_2-\ell\right]_+
+\left[L_1+L_2-\ell\right]_+ \right)
\\
&=
\begin{cases}
1\ \
& \textrm{if}\ \ 0 \le \ell \le L_2 - L_1,
\\
1-\frac{\ell}{L_1}\ \
& \textrm{if}\ \ 0 \le \ell \le L_1 - L_2,
\\
\frac{L_1+L_2-\ell}{2L_1}\ \
& \textrm{if}\ \ |L_1-L_2| \le \ell \le L_1+L_2,
\\
0\ \ 
& \textrm{if}\ \ L_1+L_2 \le \ell,
\end{cases}
\\
\sfC^{\mathrm{A}}(L_1, \ell, \ell')&=\frac{1}{L_1} \left[ L_1 - \ell - \ell' \right]_+,
\\
V\sfD^{\mathrm{A}}(L_1)&=\frac{1}{48}L_1^2,
\label{gr_kw_abcd}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $[x]_+=x$ for $x>0$ and $[x]_+=0$ for $x \le 0$. 
The kernel function $H^{\mathrm{A}}$ which provides the initial data $\sfB^{\mathrm{A}}$ and $\sfC^{\mathrm{A}}$ 
is found from $H^{\mathrm{WP}}$ in eq.\eqref{eq:H_WP} for the Weil-Petersson volume in the scaling limit such that 
\begin{align}
H^{\mathrm{A}}(x,y)=\lim_{\beta \to \infty} H^{\mathrm{WP}}(\beta x,\beta y)=
\theta(y-x)+\theta(-x-y),
\label{eq:H_A}
\end{align}
where $\theta(t)$ denotes the Heaviside step function,
\begin{align}
\theta(t)=\left\{
\begin{array}{lc}
1 & \textrm{if}\ t>0, \\
0 & \textrm{if}\ t\le 0.
\end{array}
\right.
\label{eq:Heaviside}
\end{align}

For the initial data \eqref{gr_kw_abcd}, the volume polynomial $\VO_{g,n}$ gives 
the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volume of the moduli space $\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$ of stable curves:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{A}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\exp\left(\sum_{i=1}^n \frac{L_i^2}{2}\psi_i\right)
\\
&=
\mathop{\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0}}\limits_{|\mathbf{a}|=3g-3+n}
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right)
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n}\, 
\prod_{i=1}^n e_{a_i}(L_i),
\label{kw_volume}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $e_{a}(L)$ is defined in eq.\eqref{e_base}, 
and note the homogeneity condition
\begin{align}
|\mathbf{a}|=\sum_{i=1}^n a_i = 3g-3+n.
\label{hom_kw}
\end{align}
By comparison of eq.\eqref{gr_exp} with eq.\eqref{kw_volume}, 
the volume coefficients are
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
=
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right) 
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n}.
\label{feg_kw}
\end{align}
Note that the volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{A}}$ are obtained from 
the Weil-Petersson volumes $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}$ in eq.\eqref{mir_volume} by
\begin{align}
\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{A}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\lim_{\beta \to \infty} \frac{1}{\beta^{6g-6+2n}}\, \VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}(\beta L_1,\ldots,\beta L_n),
\label{lim_a_wp}
\end{align}
and some computational results are listed in Table \ref{lst_wp} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_no_twist}.

\begin{rem}
Essentially the recursion relation \eqref{geom_rec_coeff} for the Kontsevich-Witten's symplectic volume coefficients 
is equivalent to the Dijkgraaf-Verlinde-Verlinde formula \cite{Dijkgraaf:1990rs} for the intersection numbers on the moduli space
of stable curves. 
\end{rem}


\subsubsection{$(2,p)$ minimal string}\label{subsec:gr_mg}

Let $p$ be a positive odd integer. 
The $(2,p)$ minimal string reviewed in Appendix \ref{sec:minimal} resides in a class of two dimensional gravity, 
which yields the JT gravity for $(p=\infty)$ and the topological gravity for $(p=1)$. 
Accordingly, the volume polynomial $\VO^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}$ for the $(2,p)$ minimal string interpolates
the Weil-Petersson volume $\VO^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}$ in Section \ref{subsec:gr_mir} and 
the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volume $\VO^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}$ in Section \ref{subsec:gr_kw}. 
The kernel function given below for the $(2,p)$ minimal string is derived in 
Appendix \ref{sec:derivation_minimal} from the CEO topological recursion for the spectral curve found from the physical amplitude for the disk topology ending on the FZZT brane \cite{Fateev:2000ik,Teschner:2000md,Seiberg:2003nm}. 
Here we just define it by
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,y)&=
-\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}(-1)^j\cos\left(\frac{\pi}{p}j\right)
\left(\mathrm{e}^{-u_j(x+y)}\, \theta(x+y)
+\mathrm{e}^{-u_j(x-y)}\, \theta(x-y)\right)
\\
&\quad\
+\sum_{j=0}^{(p-1)/2}(-1)^j\cos\left(\frac{\pi}{p}j\right)
\left(\mathrm{e}^{u_j(x+y)}\, \theta(-x-y)
+\mathrm{e}^{u_j(x-y)}\, \theta(y-x)\right),
\label{eq:H_minimal}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where  
\begin{align}
u_j=&\frac{p}{2\pi}\sin\left(\frac{\pi}{p}j\right).
\label{eq:uj_bosonic}
\end{align}
The kernel function \eqref{eq:H_minimal} yields
$H^{\mathrm{M}(1)}(x,y)=H^{\mathrm{A}}(x,y)$ and $H^{\mathrm{M}(\infty)}(x,y)=H^{\mathrm{WP}}(x,y)$. 
The formulae \eqref{mirz_abo_data} and \eqref{eq:DR_H_bosonic} provide 
the initial data $\sfB^{\mathrm{M}(p)}$ and $\sfC^{\mathrm{M}(p)}$ of 
the ABO topological recursion, and the remaining initial data are
\begin{align}
\sfA^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(L_1,L_2,L_3)=1,
\qquad
V\sfD^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(L_1)=\frac{\pi^2}{12}\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right) 
+ \frac{1}{48}L_1^2.
\label{gr_minimal_ad}
\end{align}
From these initial data, one finds the volume polynomials $\VO^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}$ for the $(2,p)$ minimal string, and 
some computational results are listed in 
Table \ref{lst_mst} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_no_twist}.


The following proposition is proved from the formula \eqref{mst_airy} in Section \ref{subsec:tr_mg}.

\begin{prop}\label{prop:mst_vol_poly}
The volume polynomials for the $(2,p)$ minimal string obey
\begin{align}
\VO^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\mathop{\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n \ge 0}}\limits_{|\mathbf{a}|\le 3g-3+n}
F^{\mathrm{M}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\, 
\prod_{i=1}^n e_{a_i}(L_i),
\label{gr_exp_mg}
\end{align}
where the volume coefficients are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
F^{\mathrm{M}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}&=
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right)
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}}
\exp{\left(-\sum_{b \ge 1} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b}}{b!}
\left(\prod_{k=1}^{b}\left(1-\frac{(2k-1)^2}{p^2}\right)\right)\psi^{b+1}\right)}
\\
&\hspace{27em}\times
\psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n},
\label{feg_mg}
\end{split}
\end{align}
and the condition for non-zero 
volume coefficients $F^{\mathrm{M}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ is 
$|\mathbf{a}|=\sum_{i=1}^n a_i \le 3g-3+n$.
\end{prop}


\begin{rem}
As mentioned above, the volume polynomial \eqref{gr_exp_mg} interpolates 
the Weil-Petersson volume \eqref{mir_volume} at $p=\infty$ and 
the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volume \eqref{kw_volume} at $p=1$:
\begin{align}
\VO^{\mathrm{M}(1)}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\VO^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n),
\quad
\VO^{\mathrm{M}(\infty)}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\VO^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n).
\label{v_interpolote_mp}
\end{align}
In particular, by comparison of the Weil-Petersson volume coefficients \eqref{feg_mir} with the formula \eqref{feg_mg} for $p=\infty$, we obtain 
a formula
\begin{align}
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\e^{2\pi^2 \kappa_1}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n}=
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}}
\exp{\left(-\sum_{b \ge 1} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b}}{b!}\, \psi^{b+1}\right)}
\psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n},
\label{feg_wp_formula}
\end{align}
which is found in the literature (see e.g. eq.(2.24) of \cite{Dijkgraaf:2018vnm}).
\end{rem}


\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen}
Parallel to discussions in Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa},
a deformation parameter $s$ for the volume polynomials $\VO^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}$ can be introduced by 
the replacement $\pi^2 \to \pi^2 s$ in eq.\eqref{feg_mg}.
\end{rem}




\subsection{Supersymmetric models}\label{sec:examples_gr_super}

The supersymmetric generalizations of the bosonic models are considered
as we will discuss in Appendices \ref{sec:super_models} and \ref{sec:type0A}.
We refer to a class of models such as 
the JT supergravity \cite{Stanford:2019vob}, the Br\'ezin-Gross-Witten model \cite{Gross:1980he,Brezin:1980rk,Norbury:2020vyi} in the limit of vanishing all the time variables, 
and the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring (denoted by resp. SWP, B, and SM$(p)$) as  \emph{supersymmetric models} 
(see Table \ref{tab:kernel} in Section \ref{sect:Intro}).
The super Weil-Petersson volumes \cite{Stanford:2019vob,Norbury:2020vyi} arises in a part of 
the path integral of the partition function of the JT supergravity.
In the Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion \eqref{eq:Mirzakhani's} 
for the supersymmetric models, the two functions $R(x,y,z)$ and $D(x,y,z)$ are given by a kernel function $H(x,y)$ as
\begin{align}
R(x,y,z)=\frac{1}{2}\left(H(z,x+y)+H(z,x-y)\right),
\quad
D(x,y,z)=H(y+z,x).
\label{eq:DR_H_super}
\end{align}
We will provide the kernel functions $H(x,y)$ for the supersymmetric models as well as their volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}$ in the following.



\subsubsection{Super Weil-Petersson volumes}\label{subsec:gr_sw}

The initial data of the ABO topological recursion for the super Weil-Petersson volumes\footnote{
In this article, the normalization of the super Weil-Petersson volume $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ is chosen to be identified with 
$\VO_{g,n}^{\Theta}$ defined in the Norbury's work \cite{Norbury:2020vyi}, which is the equivalent to a specialization of the Br\'ezin-Gross-Witten tau function of the KdV hierarchy. }
are \cite{Stanford:2019vob,Norbury:2020vyi},
\begin{align}
\sfA^{\mathrm{SWP}}(L_1,L_2,L_3)=0,
\qquad
V\sfD^{\mathrm{SWP}}(L_1)&=\frac{1}{8},
\label{gr_sw_abcd}
\end{align}
and the remaining ones $\sfB^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ and $\sfC^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ are found by the formulae \eqref{mirz_abo_data} and \eqref{eq:DR_H_super} from the kernel function
\begin{align}
H^{\mathrm{SWP}}(x,y)=
\frac{1}{4\pi}\left(\frac{1}{\cosh\frac{x-y}{4}}-\frac{1}{\cosh\frac{x+y}{4}}\right).
\label{eq:H_SWP}
\end{align}


For the above initial data, the volume polynomial $\VO_{g,n}$ provides 
the super Weil-Petersson volume of the moduli space of super Riemann surfaces 
which is given by the Hodge integral over the moduli space of stable curves
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} \Theta_{g,n}
\exp\left(2\pi^2 \kappa_1 + \sum_{i=1}^n \frac{L_i^2}{2}\psi_i\right),
\label{sw_volume}
\end{split}
\end{align}
and the super Weil-Petersson volume coefficients are
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{SWP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
=
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right) 
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\e^{2\pi^2 \kappa_1}\, \Theta_{g,n}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n},
\label{feg_sw}
\end{align}
where the Norbury classes $\Theta_{g,n}\in H^{4g-4+2n}(\overline{\cM}_{g,n}, \IQ)$ are defined in \cite{{Norbury:1712}}.
The super Weil-Petersson volume coefficients
$F^{\mathrm{SWP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ do not vanish, only if
\begin{align}
\sum_{i=1}^n a_i \le g-1,
\label{hom_sw}
\end{align}
and this condition implies that
$\VO_{0,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}=0$ and $\VO_{1,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}$'s are constants which do not depend on $L_i$.
Some computational results of the volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ are listed in 
Table \ref{lst_swp} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_no_twist} 
(see also \cite{Norbury:2020vyi}).


\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_kappa_super}
The super Weil-Petersson volume \eqref{sw_volume} is deformed by a change $\kappa_1\to s\kappa_1$,
and the deformed volume coefficient is found by the replacement $\pi^2 \to \pi^2 s$
in $F^{\mathrm{SWP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$.
\end{rem}



\subsubsection{Super symplectic volumes}\label{subsec:gr_be}

Using the scaling relation
\begin{align}
\label{eq:scaling_sech}
\lim_{\beta \to\infty}\frac{\beta}{\pi}\frac{1}{\cosh(\beta x)}=\delta(x),
\end{align}
one finds the kernel function for  
a supersymmetric analogue of the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes
referred to as the \emph{super symplectic volumes}:
\begin{align}
H^{\mathrm{B}}(x,y)
=\lim_{\beta \to \infty} \beta\, H^{\mathrm{SWP}}(\beta x,\beta y)
=\delta(x-y)-\delta(x+y).
\label{eq:H_B}
\end{align}
The initial data of the ABO topological recursion is given by
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\sfA^{\mathrm{B}}(L_1,L_2,L_3)&=0,
\\
\sfB^{\mathrm{B}}(L_1,L_2,\ell)&=
\frac{1}{2L_1}\,
\left(
\delta(L_1-L_2-\ell) - \delta(-L_1+L_2-\ell) + \delta(L_1+L_2-\ell)
\right),
\\
\sfC^{\mathrm{B}}(L_1, \ell, \ell')&=\frac{1}{L_1} \delta(L_1 - \ell - \ell'),
\\
V\sfD^{\mathrm{B}}(L_1)&=\frac{1}{8}.
\label{gr_be_abcd}
\end{split}
\end{align}

The volume polynomial $\VO_{g,n}$ for the initial data \eqref{gr_be_abcd} 
gives the super symplectic volume 
\cite[Proposition 6.2]{Norbury:2020vyi}:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{B}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} \Theta_{g,n}
\exp\left(\sum_{i=1}^n \frac{L_i^2}{2}\psi_i\right)
\\
&=
\mathop{\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0}}\limits_{|\mathbf{a}|=g-1}
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right) 
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\Theta_{g,n}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n}\, 
\prod_{i=1}^n e_{a_i}(L_i),
\label{be_volume}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where note the homogeneity condition
\begin{align}
|\mathbf{a}|=\sum_{i=1}^n a_i = (3g-3+n) - (2g-2+n) = g-1.
\label{hom_be}
\end{align}
By comparison of eq.\eqref{gr_exp} with eq.\eqref{be_volume}, 
the volume coefficients are
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{B}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
=
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right) 
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\Theta_{g,n}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n}.
\label{feg_be}
\end{align}
Note that some of the volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{B}}$ are found from 
the super Weil-Petersson volumes $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ in 
Table \ref{lst_swp} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_no_twist} by
\begin{align}
\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{B}}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\lim_{\beta \to \infty} \frac{1}{\beta^{2g-2}}\, \VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}(\beta L_1,\ldots,\beta L_n),
\label{lim_b_swp}
\end{align}
or from the volume polynomials $\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}$ for 
the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring below in eq.\eqref{vol_minimal_superstring} by $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{B}}=\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(1)}_{g,n}$.



\subsubsection{$(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring}\label{subsec:gr_mg_super}


Here we will consider a family of ABO recursions interpolating the ABO topological recursions of super Weil-Petersson volumes in Section \ref{subsec:gr_sw} and super symplectic volumes in Section \ref{subsec:gr_be},
and such model is regarded as the type 0A $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring (see the physical interpretations in Appendix \ref{sec:type0A}).
A supersymmetric analogue model is found from an interpolation of the spectral curves for the CEO topological recursions
(see Appendix \ref{sec:type0A} for its derivation), 
and the kernel function in the Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion for 
the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring is derived in Appendix \ref{sec:derivation_super_minimal}. 
Here we just define the kernel function  by
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
H^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(x,y)&=
\frac{1}{2\pi}\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}(-1)^j
\cos^2\left(\frac{\pi}{p}\left(j-\frac{1}{2}\right)\right)
\Bigl(\mathrm{e}^{-u'_j(x+y)}\, \theta(x+y)
-\mathrm{e}^{-u'_j(x-y)}\, \theta(x-y)
\\
&\hspace{16em}
+\mathrm{e}^{u'_j(x+y)}\, \theta(-x-y)
-\mathrm{e}^{u'_j(x-y)}\, \theta(y-x)\Bigr)
\\
&\quad
+\left(\delta(x-y)-\delta(x+y)\right)\delta_{p,1},
\label{eq:H_super_minimal}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where
\begin{align}
u'_j=&\frac{p}{2\pi}\sin\left(\frac{\pi}{p}\left(j-\frac{1}{2}\right)\right).
\label{eq:uj_super}
\end{align}
This kernel function obeys 
$H^{\mathrm{SM}(1)}(x,y)=H^{\mathrm{B}}(x,y)$ and $H^{\mathrm{SM}(\infty)}(x,y)=H^{\mathrm{SWP}}(x,y)$.
From the formulae \eqref{mirz_abo_data} and \eqref{eq:DR_H_super}, 
the initial data $\sfB^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}$ and $\sfC^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}$ 
of the ABO topological recursion are obtained, and the remaining ones are
\begin{align}
\sfA^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(L_1,L_2,L_3)=0,
\qquad
V\sfD^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(L_1)=\frac18.
\label{gr_superminimal_ad}
\end{align}
Using the initial data,
one can compute the volume polynomials $\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}$ for 
the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring iteratively.
In particular for the supersymmetric model, the recursion for the volume coefficients simplifies drastically,
and the general form of the volume polynomials for any odd $p$ is obtained for $g=0,1,2,3$ as follows:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{0,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=0,\qquad
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=\frac{(n-1)!}{8},
\\
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\frac{3(n+1)!}{128}
\bigg[(n+2)\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)\pi^2
+ \frac14 \sum_{i=1}^n L_i^2\bigg],
\\
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{3,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\frac{(n+3)!}{2^{16}\cdot 5}
\bigg[16(n+4)\left(42n\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)+185+\frac{15}{p^2}\right)
\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)\pi^4
\\
&\hspace{4.5em}
+336(n+4)\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)\pi^2\, \sum_{i=1}^nL_i^2
+84\sum_{i \ne j}^n L_i^2 L_j^2
+25\sum_{i=1}^n L_i^4\bigg].
\label{vol_minimal_superstring}
\end{split}
\end{align}
More computational results are listed in 
Table \ref{lst_super_mst} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_no_twist}.


Similar to Proposition \ref{prop:mst_vol_poly}, the following proposition is proved from the formula \eqref{msst_bessel} in Section \ref{subsec:tr_mg_super}.

\begin{prop}\label{prop:mst_vol_poly_super}
The volume polynomials for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring obey
\begin{align}
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\mathop{\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n \ge 0}}\limits_{|\mathbf{a}|\le g-1}
F^{\mathrm{SM}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\, 
\prod_{i=1}^n e_{a_i}(L_i),
\label{gr_exp_smg}
\end{align}
where the volume coefficients are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
F^{\mathrm{SM}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}&=
\left(\prod_{i=1}^n(2a_i+1)!!\right)
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}}
\exp{\left(-\sum_{b \ge 1} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b}}{b!}
\left(\prod_{k=1}^{b}\left(1-\frac{(2k-1)^2}{p^2}\right)\right)\psi^{b}\right)}
\\
&\hspace{25em}\times
\Theta_{g,n}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n},
\label{feg_smg}
\end{split}
\end{align}
and do not vanish only if
$|\mathbf{a}|=\sum_{i=1}^n a_i \le g-1$.
\end{prop}

\begin{rem}
The volume polynomial \eqref{gr_exp_smg} interpolates 
the super Weil-Petersson volume \eqref{sw_volume} at $p=\infty$ and 
the super symplectic volume \eqref{be_volume} at $p=1$:
\begin{align}
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(1)}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\VO^{\mathrm{B}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n),
\quad
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(\infty)}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\VO^{\mathrm{SWP}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n).
\label{v_interpolote_mp_super}
\end{align}
In particular, by comparing the super Weil-Petersson volume coefficients \eqref{feg_sw} with the formula \eqref{feg_smg} for $p=\infty$, we obtain 
a super analogue of the formula \eqref{feg_wp_formula}:
\begin{align}
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}} 
\e^{2\pi^2 \kappa_1}\, \Theta_{g,n}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n}=
\int_{\overline{\cM}_{g,n}}
\exp{\left(-\sum_{b \ge 1} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b}}{b!}\psi^{b}\right)}
\Theta_{g,n}\, \psi_1^{a_1} \cdots \psi_n^{a_n}.
\label{feg_wp_formula_super}
\end{align}
Note that the power of $\psi$ in the exponent on the right hand side is shifted by one 
compared to the formula \eqref{feg_wp_formula}.
\end{rem}


\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen_super}
A deformation parameter $s$ for the volume polynomials $\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}$ can also be introduced by 
the replacement $\pi^2 \to \pi^2 s$ in eq.\eqref{feg_smg}.
\end{rem}


\subsection{ABO topological recursion with twist}\label{sec:twisting_gr}

Here we will consider the twist action of the ABO topological recursion \cite{Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV}.
The twisting of the ABO topological recursion is originated from the study of the statistics of length of multicurves in a connected bordered Riemann surface, which leads to the combinatorial computation of the Masur-Veech volume \cite{Masur,Veech} for the moduli space of quadratic differentials on Riemann surfaces.
To discuss this aspect of the ABO topological recursion, we summarize a working definition of 
stable graphs \cite{Mirz_MV} (see \cite[Appendix B]{DGZZ_latest} for a formal definition of stable graphs).

Let $\gamma_i$ ($i=1,\ldots,k$) be simple closed geodesics on a bordered surface $S_{g,n}$ of genus $g$ with $n$ boundary components.
We assume that $\gamma_i$ and $\gamma_j$ ($i\ne j$) are pairwise non-isotopic with regard to the action of the mapping class group 
$\mathrm{Mod}_{g,n}$ on $S_{g,n}$ and not intersecting each other 
(see Figure \ref{fig:multi_curve} (left) for an example).
\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{0cm}
\hspace*{-5cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=50mm]{multi_curve.pdf}
 \vspace{0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:multi_curve}
Left: Two simple closed geodesics $\gamma_1,\gamma_2$ in $S_{1,2}$.
Right: Decomposition of $S_{1,2}$ cut by $\gamma_1,\gamma_2$.
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
A multicurve $\gamma$ is given  by
\begin{align}
\label{eq:multicurve}
\gamma=\sum_{i=1}^kH_i\gamma_i,
\end{align}
where $(H_1,\ldots,H_k)$ is a set of positive integers and $\gamma_i$'s are disjoint, essential, non-peripheral simple closed curves in $S_{g,n}$.
For the above multicurve $\gamma$, the reduced multicurve $\gamma_{\mathrm{red}}$ is $\gamma_{\mathrm{red}}=\sum_{i=1}^k\gamma_i$.



A \emph{stable graph} $\Gamma$ is associated with the pair 
$(S_{g,n},\gamma_{\mathrm{red}})$ by cutting a bordered surface $S_{g,n}$ 
along a reduced multicurve $\gamma_{\mathrm{red}}$ such that
\begin{align}
\label{eq:cut_Riemann_surface}
S_{g,n}\setminus\gamma_{\mathrm{red}}=
\bigsqcup_{a=1}^{N} S_{g_a,n_a},
\end{align}
where $S_{g_a,n_a}$'s are connected stable bordered surfaces with $2g_a-2+n_a>0$.
For example, a decomposition $S_{1,2}\setminus\{\gamma_1,\gamma_2\}$ is found in Figure \ref{fig:multi_curve} (right).
The associated stable graph $\Gamma$ is the dual decorated graph 
made of decorated vertices $v_a$ and edges $e_i$ found from the decomposition \eqref{eq:cut_Riemann_surface} as in Figure \ref{fig:stable_graph_components}. The basic data of the stable graph are given as follows:
\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{2.5cm}
\hspace*{-6cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=70mm]{stable_graph_components.pdf}
 \vspace{0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:stable_graph_components}
Top: Identification of $S_{g,n}$ with 
an $n$-valent vertex decorated by an integer $g$ of the stable graph.
Bottom: Identification of a decomposition of a bordered surface with 
an edge and half-edges of a stable graph.
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
\begin{itemize}
\item 
Vertex $v_a$ ($a=1,\ldots,N$): 
an $n_a$-valent vertex decorated by an integer $g_a$ associated with $S_{g_a,n_a}$ ;
\item 
Internal edge $e_i$ ($i=1,\ldots,k$): 
an edge associated with the simple closed curve $\gamma_i$ ;
\item 
Incidence relation: 
two vertices $v_a, v_b$ are connected by an edge $e_i$ if 
$S_{g_a,n_a}$ and $S_{g_b,n_b}$ are adjacent to a simple closed curve $\gamma_i$ in $S_{g,n}$ s.t.
$S_{g_a,n_a}\sqcup_{\gamma_i}S_{g_b,n_b}\subset S_{g,n}$, 
where the edge $e_i$ forms a loop in the stable graph for the case of $a=b$;
\item 
Half-edge $b_p$ ($p=1,\ldots,n$): a half-edge associated with bordered boundaries in $S_{g,n}$.
\end{itemize}
We denote by $G_{g,n}$ the set of stable graphs associated with $S_{g,n}$, 
and by $\mathsf{V}_{\Gamma}$ and $\mathsf{E}_{\Gamma}$ 
the sets of edges and vertices in $\Gamma \in G_{g,n}$, respectively.



\begin{Def}[Twisted volume polynomials \cite{Andersen_GR}]\label{def:tw_abo_amp}
Let $\sff:\ {\IR}_+ \to {\IC}$ be an \emph{admissible test function}, 
i.e. a Riemann-integrable function on $\IR_+$ 
such that 
\begin{align}
\mathop{\sup}\limits_{\ell>0}\, (1+\ell)^s |\sff(\ell)|<\infty
\qquad
\textrm{for any } s>0.
\end{align}
The \emph{twisted volume polynomials} $\VO_{g,n}[\sff]$ are defined as the combinations of the volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}$ on basis of the basic data of the stable graphs by
(see \cite[Lemma 7.4]{Andersen_GR}),
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\label{eq:twist_volume}
\VO_{g,n}[\sff](L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\sum_{\Gamma\in G_{g,n}} \frac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)|}
\int_{\IR_+^{|\mathsf{E}_{\Gamma}|}} 
\prod_{v\in \mathsf{V}_{\Gamma}}
\VO_{h(v),k(v)}\bigl((\ell_e)_{e\in\mathsf{E}(v)},
(L_{\lambda})_{\lambda\in\Lambda(v)}\bigr)
\\
&\hspace{10em}\times
\prod_{e\in \mathsf{E}_{\Gamma}} \sff(\ell_e)\, \ell_e d\ell_e,
\end{split}
\end{align}
where  $\mathsf{E}(v)$ and $\Lambda(v)$ denote 
the sets of edges and half-edges emanating from a vertex 
$v\in \mathsf{V}_{\Gamma}$, respectively.
The expansion \eqref{gr_exp} for $\VO_{g,n}[\sff]$ defines
the \emph{twisted volume coefficients} $F^{(g)}[\sff]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$:
\begin{align}
V_{g,n}[\sff](L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n\ge 0} F^{(g)}[\sff]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\, 
\prod_{i=1}^n e_{a_i}(L_i),
\label{eq:expansion_volume}
\end{align}
where $e_{a}(L)=L^{2a}/(2a+1)!$.
\end{Def}


\begin{prop}[Twisted initial data \cite{Andersen_GR}]\label{def:twist}
The twisted volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}[\sff]$ are 
obtained from the ABO topological recursion with the following 
four twisted initial data $(\sfA[\sff], \sfB[\sff], \sfC[\sff], \sfD[\sff])$:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\sfA[\sff](L_1, L_2, L_3)&=\sfA(L_1, L_2, L_3),
\\
\sfB[\sff](L_1, L_2, \ell)&=\sfB(L_1, L_2, \ell) + \sfA(L_1, L_2, \ell)\, \sff(\ell),
\\
\sfC[\sff](L_1, \ell, \ell')&=\sfC(L_1, \ell, \ell')
+ \sfB(L_1, \ell, \ell')\, \sff(\ell) + \sfB(L_1, \ell', \ell)\, \sff(\ell')
+ \sfA(L_1, \ell, \ell')\, \sff(\ell)\, \sff(\ell'),
\\
\sfD[\sff](\sigma)&=\sfD(\sigma)
+\frac12 \sum_{\gamma \in S_T^{\circ}}
\sfA(\ell_{\sigma}(\partial T), \ell_{\sigma}(\gamma), 
\ell_{\sigma}(\gamma))\, \sff(\ell_{\sigma}(\gamma)),
\label{abcd_twist}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $S_T^{\circ}$ is the set of simple closed curves in a torus with one boundary $T$.
$\ell_{\sigma}(\partial T)$ and $\ell_{\sigma}(\gamma)$ denote the lengths of the boundary $\partial T$ 
and the shortest geodesic in the homotopy class of $\gamma$ with respect to a hyperbolic metric $\sigma$ on $T$, respectively.
\end{prop}


From eqs.\eqref{gr_coeff_bc} and \eqref{geom_rec_coeff_ini}, 
the twisted initial data \eqref{abcd_twist} imply
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\sfA[\sff]^{a_1}_{a_2,a_3}&=\sfA^{a_1}_{a_2,a_3},
\\
\sfB[\sff]^{a_1}_{a_2,a_3}&=\sfB^{a_1}_{a_2,a_3}
+ \sum_{a \ge 0} \sfA^{a_1}_{a_2,a}\, u_{a, a_3},
\\
\sfC[\sff]^{a_1}_{a_2,a_3}&=\sfC^{a_1}_{a_2,a_3}
+ \sum_{a \ge 0} 
\left(\sfB^{a_1}_{a,a_2}\, u_{a, a_3} + \sfB^{a_1}_{a,a_3}\, u_{a, a_2}\right)
+ \sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfA^{a_1}_{a,b}\, u_{a, a_2}\, u_{b, a_3},
\\
\sfD[\sff]^{a_1}&=\sfD^{a_1}
+\frac12 \sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfA^{a_1}_{a,b}\, u_{a,b},
\label{vir_abcd_twist}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where
\begin{align}
u_{a, b}= 
u[\sff]_{a, b}= 
\int_{\IR_+} \frac{\ell^{2a + 2b +1}}
{\left(2a+1\right)!\left(2b+1\right)!}\, \sff(\ell)\, d\ell.
\label{twist_u}
\end{align}
In particular, we consider the Masur-Veech type twist,
\begin{align}
\sfm(\ell)=\frac{1}{\e^{\ell}-1},
\label{mv_twist}
\end{align}
as an admissible test function, and then the twist function \eqref{twist_u} is
\begin{align}
u_{a, b}^{\mathrm{MV}}=
u[\sfm]_{a, b}=
\frac{\left(2a+2b+1\right)!}{\left(2a+1\right)!\left(2b+1\right)!}\, 
\zeta(2a+2b+2).
\label{mv_twist_u}
\end{align}



\subsection{Masur-Veech type twist}\label{sec:examples_gr_tw}

Here we focus on the Masur-Veech type twist of 
the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes in Section \ref{subsec:gr_kw},
the volume polynomials for the $(2,p)$ minimal string in Section \ref{subsec:gr_mg},
the super symplectic volumes in Section \ref{subsec:gr_be} and
the volume polynomials for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring in Section \ref{subsec:gr_mg_super}.
In the following, we will summarize the computational results of the volume polynomials with the Masur-Veech type twist.

\subsubsection{Masur-Veech polynomials}\label{subsec:gr_mvp}

In \cite{Andersen_MV}, it is shown that the constant terms of 
the twisted Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes
\begin{align}
V^{\mathrm{MV}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n):=
V^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n),
\label{mv_tw_kw}
\end{align}
which are referred to as the \emph{Masur-Veech polynomials}, 
give the Masur-Veech volumes 
$\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ reviewed in Section \ref{sec_MV_stable} 
(see eq.\eqref{eq:Masur-Veech_twisted}). 
Some computational results of the Masur-Veech polynomials are 
listed in Table \ref{lst_mv} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}.




\subsubsection{Twisted volume polynomials for $(2,p)$ minimal string}\label{subsec:gr_mg_twisted}

The twisted volume polynomial $\VO^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ for the $(2,p)$ minimal string interpolates the Masur-Veech polynomial $V^{\mathrm{MV}}_{g,n}$ in eq.\eqref{mv_tw_kw} at $p=1$ and the twisted Weil-Petersson volume 
$\VO^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ at $p=\infty$:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\VO^{\mathrm{M}(1)}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\VO^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\VO^{\mathrm{MV}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n),
\\
\VO^{\mathrm{M}(\infty)}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\VO^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n).
\label{v_interpolote_mp_tw}
\end{split}
\end{align}
Some of the twisted Weil-Petersson volumes 
$\VO^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ and 
the twisted volume polynomial $\VO^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ are 
listed in Table \ref{lst_wp_tw_s} and \ref{lst_mst_twist_s} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}, respectively, 
where the deformation parameter $s$ is introduced following 
Remarks \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa} and \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen}.
A combinatorial formula for the constant term of $\VO^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ is provided in Proposition \ref{prop:minimal_combi} of Section \ref{sec:combi_minimal}.



\subsubsection{Super Masur-Veech polynomials}\label{subsec:gr_supermvp}

As a supersymmetric analogue of the Masur-Veech polynomials \eqref{mv_tw_kw}, 
we define the \emph{super Masur-Veech polynomials} by
\begin{align}
V^{\mathrm{SMV}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n):=
V^{\mathrm{B}}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n).
\label{smv_tw_bessel}
\end{align}
Some computational results are listed in Table \ref{lst_smv} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}, or 
found from the twisted volume polynomials 
$\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring 
below in eq.\eqref{vol_minimal_superstring_twist} by a specialization
$V^{\mathrm{SMV}}_{g,n}=\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(1)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$.



\subsubsection{Twisted volume polynomials for $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring}\label{subsec:gr_mg_super_twisted}

For the twisted volume polynomials 
$\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring, 
the twisted ABO topological recursion is solve iteratively, 
and the general form of $\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ for any odd $p$ is obtained for $g=0,1,2,3$ as follows:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{0,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)=0,\qquad
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)=\frac{(n-1)!}{8},
\\
&
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\frac{3(n+1)!}{128}
\bigg[(n+2)\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}+\frac12\right)\pi^2
+ \frac14 \sum_{i=1}^n L_i^2\bigg],
\\
&
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{3,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)
\\
&=
\frac{(n+3)!}{2^{16}\cdot 5}
\bigg[\bigg\{16(n+4)\left(42n\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)+\frac{455}{2}+\frac{15}{p^2}\right)
\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)+\frac{23\cdot 40}{3}\bigg\}\pi^4
\\
&\hspace{4.5em}
+\bigg\{336(n+4)\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)+170\bigg\}\pi^2\, \sum_{i=1}^nL_i^2
+84\sum_{i \ne j}^n L_i^2 L_j^2
+25\sum_{i=1}^n L_i^4\bigg].
\label{vol_minimal_superstring_twist}
\end{split}
\end{align}
More computational results are listed in Table \ref{lst_super_mst_twist_s} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}, 
where the deformation parameter $s$ is introduced following Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen_super}. 
The twisted volume polynomial $\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ interpolates 
the super Masur-Veech polynomial $V^{\mathrm{SMV}}_{g,n}$ in eq.\eqref{smv_tw_bessel} at $p=1$ and the twisted super Weil-Petersson volume 
$\VO^{\mathrm{SWP}}_{g,n}[\sfm]$ at $p=\infty$ summarized in Table \ref{lst_super_wp_tw_s} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist} such that
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(1)}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\VO^{\mathrm{B}}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)=
\VO^{\mathrm{SMV}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n),
\\
\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(\infty)}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)&=
\VO^{\mathrm{SWP}}_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n).
\label{v_interpolote_mp_tw_super}
\end{split}
\end{align}
In Proposition \ref{prop:minimal_super_combi} of Section \ref{sec:combi_super}, 
we find a combinatorial formula for the constant term of $\VO^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm]$.





%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{The Masur-Veech volume and its generalizations}\label{sect:MasurVeech}

In this section, we will discuss generalizations of the Masur-Veech volume of quadratic differentials on a complex curve with marked points, and compute them for some examples on basis of the Mirzakhani's combinatorial reformulation. 

\subsection{Combinatorial formula for the Masur-Veech volume}\label{sec_MV_stable}

To begin with, we summarize essential ingredients on the Masur-Veech volume of quadratic differentials discussed in \cite{DGZZ_latest} shortly.
Let $\mathcal{M}_{g,n}$ be the moduli space of complex curves of genus $g$ with $n$ distinct labeled marked points.
On a smooth complex curve $C\in \mathcal{M}_{g,n}$, 
consider a meromorphic quadratic differential $q$ which would have 
at most simple poles only at the marked points 
and is not equal to the square of an Abelian differential.
The moduli space of pairs $(q,C)$ on $\mathcal{M}_{g,n}$ defines the cotangent bundle over $\mathcal{M}_{g,n}$,
and the \emph{moduli space of quadratic differentials} $\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ is identified with 
the total space of the cotangent bundle over $\mathcal{M}_{g,n}$ endowed with the canonical symplectic structure.
The induced volume element on $\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ is called the \emph{Masur-Veech volume element}.%
\footnote{
The finiteness of the Masur-Veech volume element for a subset 
$\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{Area}(C,q)\le a}_{g,n}$ of $\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$:
$$
\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{Area}(C,q)\le a}_{g,n}=\bigg\{
(C,q)\in \mathcal{Q}_{g,n}\; \bigg|\; \mathrm{Area}(C,q)=\int_C|q|\le a
\bigg\}
\subset \mathcal{Q}_{g,n},
$$
with the total area $\mathrm{Area}(C,q)$ smaller than $a>0$ is confirmed by the independent results of Masur \cite{Masur} and Veech \cite{Veech}.
}


\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{0cm}
\hspace*{-2cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=50mm]{stratification.pdf}
 \vspace{0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:stratification}
The label set $\mu=(\mu_1,\ldots,\mu_m)$ in the stratum $\mathcal{Q}(\mu)$ of 
quadratic differentials on a complex curve of genus $g$ with $m$ distinct labeled marked points.
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}


The moduli space $\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ is naturally stratified by the multiplicities of zeros and poles of quadratic differentials.


\begin{Def}[Stratum of quadratic differentials]
The stratum $\mathcal{Q}(\mu)$ of quadratic differentials is the set of equivalence classes of pairs: 
a smooth complex curve $C$ with $m$ marked points $p_i$ $(i=1,\ldots,m)$ and a quadratic differential $q$ with divisor $D=\sum_{i=1}^m\mu_ip_i$.
Here $\mu=(\mu_1,\ldots,\mu_m)$ is a label set satisfying 
(see Figure \ref{fig:stratification}),
\begin{align}
\label{eq:MV_stratum}
\mu_i\ge -1\;(i=1,\ldots,m),
\qquad \sum_{i=1}^{m}\mu_i=4g-4,
\end{align}
where $\mu_i=-1$ implies a simple pole. 
The stratum $\mathcal{Q}(\mu)$ is a complex orbifold of dimension 
$\dim_{\IC}\mathcal{Q}(\mu)=2g-2+m$ \cite{Veech_mod}.
\end{Def}


In particular, we consider the principal stratum $\mathcal{Q}(1^{4g-4+n},-1^n)$ of meromorphic quadratic differentials on 
$C \in \mathcal{M}_{g,4g-4+2n}$. 
The fibers of $\mathcal{Q}(1^{4g-4+n},-1^n) \to \mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ are discrete, 
and the forgetful morphism $\mathcal{Q}_{g,4g-4+2n} \to \mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ of 
the $4g-4+n$ marked points gives a bijection between 
the principal stratum $\mathcal{Q}(1^{4g-4+n},-1^n)$ modulo the choice of 
$4g-4+n$ marked points and the moduli space $\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$.
The dimension of the principal stratum coincides with that of $\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$: $\dim_{\mathbb{C}}\mathcal{Q}(1^{4g-4+n},-1^n)=\dim_{\mathbb{C}}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}=6g-6+2n$. We denote the Masur-Veech volume of the principal stratum $\mathcal{Q}(1^{4g-4+n},-1^n)$ as $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$.


In the work by Mirzakhani \cite{Mirz_MV}, the Masur-Veech volume $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ is reformulated as an enumerative problem of the simple closed curves in a connected bordered (hyperbolic) Riemann surface, 
and a connection with the Weil-Petersson volume is found. 
This reformulation is established further on basis of the enumerative problem of square-tiled surfaces in the work by Delecroix, Goujard, Zograf and Zorich \cite{DGZZ_latest}.
By such reformulations, a relation between the Masur-Veech volume of the moduli space of quadratic differentials and the intersection number on the (compactified) moduli space $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ is unveiled.
The stable graphs $\Gamma \in G_{g,n}$ associated with a bordered surface $S_{g,n}$ and a reduced multicurve $\gamma_{\mathrm{red}}$ 
in Section \ref{sec:twisting_gr} are used in the combinatorial computation of 
the Masur-Veech volume $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$.


\begin{thm}[Combinatorial formula for the Masur-Veech volume \cite{Mirz_MV,DGZZ_latest}]\label{thm_combi_MV}
Consider a decomposition \eqref{eq:cut_Riemann_surface} associated to a stable graph $\Gamma$
for a bordered Riemann surface $S_{g,n}$, and 
set all boundary lengths $L_p$ ($p=1,\ldots n$) of the original bordered Riemann surface to zero 
in each connected piece.
Define a polynomial
\begin{align}
\label{eq:polynomial_WP}
\mathrm{Vol}^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_k):=
\prod_{a=1}^N \widetilde{V}^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g_a,n_a}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_{k_a}),
\end{align}
where $\widetilde{V}^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g_a,n_a}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_{k_a})$ denote the Weil-Petersson volumes of moduli spaces of connected piece of bordered Riemann surfaces obtained by a decomposition represented by $\Gamma$.
Let $(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma}$ denote the coefficient of $\ell_1^{2d_1}\cdots \ell_k^{2d_k}$ in $\mathrm{Vol}^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_k)$.
From these combinatorial data,
the Masur-Veech volume $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$ of the moduli space of quadratic differentials is given by%
\footnote{
In \cite{Mirz_MV,DGZZ_latest}, an extra factor $2^{-M(\gamma)}$ appears in  eq.\eqref{comb_formula_mv} originated from the normalization for the Weil-Petersson volume $V_{1,1}^{\mathrm{WP}}(L)$ in Table 1 of \cite{Mirz3}. 
In this article, we employ another normalization $V_{1,1}^{\mathrm{WP}}(L)$ obtained from the CEO topological recursion
which is different by factor $2$ from the Mirzakhani's original computation.
}
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\label{comb_formula_mv}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}
&=\sum_{\Gamma\in G_{g,n}}
\frac{\alpha_{g,n}}{|\mathrm{Aut}\left(\Gamma\right)|}
\sum_{|\mathbf{d}|= 3g-3+n-k}(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma}\,
\frac{\prod_{i=1}^k(2d_i+1)!}{(6g-6+2n)!}
\prod_{i=1}^k\zeta(2d_i+2),
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $|\mathbf{d}|=\sum_{i=1}^kd_i$, and the normalization constant $\alpha_{g,n}$ is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:normalization_MV}
\alpha_{g,n}:=2\cdot(6g-6+2n)\cdot(4g-4+n)!\cdot 2^{4g-3+n}.
\end{align}
\end{thm}


\begin{rem}
The normalization constant $\alpha_{g,n}$ in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_MV} is obtained in a series of works \cite{AH1,MoT,ErSo,Wr}.
\end{rem}


\begin{rem}
Let $\mathrm{Vol}^{\mathrm{A}}_{\Gamma}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_k)$ 
be a polynomial defined by replacing the Weil-Petersson volumes 
in eq.\eqref{eq:polynomial_WP} with the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes 
of moduli spaces of stable curves in eq.\eqref{kw_volume}, 
and $(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)^{\mathrm{A}}_{\Gamma}$ be 
the coefficient of  $\ell_1^{2d_1}\cdots \ell_k^{2d_k}$ in $\mathrm{Vol}^{\mathrm{A}}_{\Gamma}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_k)$. 
The combinatorial formula \eqref{comb_formula_mv} also holds if $(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma}$ is replaced with $(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)^{\mathrm{A}}_{\Gamma}$.
\end{rem}

The following proposition is shown in \cite{Andersen_MV}.

\begin{prop}[\cite{Andersen_MV}]\label{prop:mv_twisted_abo}
The Masur-Veech volumes is found from the constant terms in the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes with the Masur-Veech type twist in eq.\eqref{mv_twist}:
\begin{align}
\label{eq:Masur-Veech_twisted}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}
=\beta_{g,n}\,
V^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}[\sfm](0,\ldots,0)
=\beta_{g,n}\,
V^{\mathrm{MV}}_{g,n}(0,\ldots,0),
\end{align}
where the normalization constant $\beta_{g,n}$ is
\begin{align}
&\label{eq:volume_factor}
\beta_{g,n}:=\frac{2^{4g-2+n}\, (4g-4+n)!}{(6g-7+2n)!}.
\end{align}
\end{prop}
\begin{proof}
The integrals of $\ell_e$ in eq.\eqref{eq:twist_volume} 
give the factors involving $\zeta(2d_i+2)$ 
in the combinatorial formula \eqref{comb_formula_mv} for the Masur-Veech volumes.
As a result, the collection of the monomials with degree $|\mathbf{d}|= 3g-3+n-k$ in $V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{g,n}$ agrees with that of $V^{\mathrm{A}}_{g,n}$.
\end{proof}

For example, the Masur-Veech volumes $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{1,1}$ and $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{0,4}$ are computed as follows.
(A huge table of the Masur-Veech volumes is obtained in \cite{Goujard15}.)

\begin{ex}[$g=1, n=1$]
One finds a decomposition \eqref{eq:cut_Riemann_surface} which splits $S_{1,1}$ into one $S_{0,3}$, and obtains a stable graph $\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)}$ as described in Figure \ref{fig:stable_graph_MV} (top).
\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{3.5cm}
\hspace*{-6cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=50mm]{multi_curve_MV.pdf}
 \vspace{0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:stable_graph_MV}
Top: A stable graph $\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)}$ from $(S_{1,1},\gamma_1)$.
Bottom: A stable graph $\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)}$ from $(S_{0,4},\gamma_1)$,
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
A discrete $\mathbb{Z}/2\mathbb{Z}$ symmetry of a loop is found in this stable graph, and 
$\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)})\big|=2$.
The polynomial \eqref{eq:polynomial_WP} for this decomposition is $\mathrm{Vol}^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)}}(x)
=V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{0,3}(x,x,0)=1$.
Therefore, $k=1$, $d_1=0$ and $(2d_1)^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)}}=1$ for this stable graph contributes to the sum in eq.\eqref{comb_formula_mv}, 
and one finds 
\begin{align}
\label{MV_volume_11}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{1,1}
=\frac{\alpha_{1,1}}{\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)})\big|}\,
