(2d_1)^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)}}\, \frac{(2d_1+1)!}{2!}\,
\zeta(2d_1+2)
=\frac{2\pi^2}{3}.
\end{align}
This agrees with 
$\beta_{1,1}V^{\mathrm{MV}}_{1,1}(0)=2^3\cdot \pi^2/12$ in 
eq.\eqref{eq:Masur-Veech_twisted} 
(see Table \ref{lst_mv} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}).
\end{ex}


\begin{ex}[$g=0, n=4$]
One finds a decomposition \eqref{eq:cut_Riemann_surface} which splits $S_{0,4}$ into two $S_{0,3}$'s, and obtain a stable graph $\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)}$ as described in Figure \ref{fig:stable_graph_MV} (bottom).
There are $\binom{4}{2}=6$ choices of the distribution of four labeled external legs into two $S_{0,3}$'s in this case.
A discrete $\mathbb{Z}/2\mathbb{Z}$ symmetry of the stable graph 
$\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)}$ leads to $\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)})\big|=2$.
The polynomial \eqref{eq:polynomial_WP} for this decomposition is $\mathrm{Vol}^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)}}(x)=V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{0,3}(x,0,0)\cdot V^{\mathrm{WP}}_{0,3}(x,0,0)=1$.
Therefore, $k=1$, $d_1=0$ and $(2d_1)^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)}}=1$ for this stable graph contributes to the sum in eq.\eqref{comb_formula_mv}, and one finds 
\begin{align}
\label{MV_volume_04}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{0,4}=
\frac{\alpha_{0,4}}{\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)})\big|}\,
\binom{4}{2}\,
(2d_1)^{\mathrm{WP}}_{\Gamma^{(1)}}\, \frac{(2d_1+1)!}{2!}\,
\zeta(2d_1+2)
=2\pi^2.
\end{align}
This agrees with 
$\beta_{0,4}V^{\mathrm{MV}}_{0,4}(0,0,0,0)=2^2\cdot \pi^2/2$ in 
eq.\eqref{eq:Masur-Veech_twisted} 
(see Table \ref{lst_mv} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}).
\end{ex}



\subsection{Generalizations of the combinatorial formula: $(2,p)$ minimal strings}\label{sec:combi_minimal}

Now we consider a generalization of the combinatorial formula \eqref{comb_formula_mv} to the $(2,p)$ minimal string
whose volume polynomials interpolate the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes (for $p=1$) and 
the Weil-Petersson volumes (for $p=\infty$).
For this purpose, we consider a stable graph $\Gamma \in G_{g,n}$ associated to 
a pair $(S_{g,n},\gamma_{\mathrm{red}})$ of the decomposition \eqref{eq:cut_Riemann_surface} in Section \ref{sec:twisting_gr}, 
and define
\begin{align}
(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)_{\Gamma}=
\textrm{the coefficient of}\ \ell_1^{2d_1}\cdots \ell_k^{2d_k}\ 
\textrm{in}\
\prod_{a=1}^N \widetilde{V}_{g_a,n_a}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_{k_a}).
\label{vol_component_comb}
\end{align}
Here $\widetilde{V}_{g_a,n_a}(\ell_1,\ldots,\ell_{k_a})$ are 
the volume polynomials associated with the stable graph $\Gamma$ 
and with zero boundary lengths $L_p=0$ ($p=1,\ldots n$) for the bordered boundaries in the decomposed Riemann surfaces
specified by the univalent vertices in $\Gamma$. Then, the following proposition is proved.


\begin{prop}[Combinatorial formula for the twisted volume of $(2,p)$ minimal strings]\label{prop:minimal_combi} 
The constant term in the twisted volume polynomial
$V^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ 
of the $(2,p)$ minimal string normalized by $\beta_{g,n}$ in eq.\eqref{eq:volume_factor},
\begin{align}
\label{eq:minimal_twisted}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}=
\beta_{g,n}\,
V^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](0,\ldots,0),
\end{align}
is obtained, as a sum over the stable graphs $\Gamma\in G_{g,n}$, by
\begin{align}
\label{eq:normalization_minimal_volume}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}
=\sum_{\Gamma\in G_{g,n}}
\frac{\alpha_{g,n}}{|\mathrm{Aut}\left(\Gamma\right)|}
\sum_{|\mathbf{d}|\le 3g-3+n-k}(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)_{\Gamma}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}\,
\frac{\prod_{i=1}^k(2d_i+1)!}{(6g-6+2n)!}
\prod_{i=1}^k\zeta(2d_i+2),
\end{align}
in terms of $(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)_{\Gamma}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}$ defined by eq.\eqref{vol_component_comb} for the $(2,p)$ minimal string, 
where the normalization factor $\alpha_{g,n}$ is the same as eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_MV}.
We refer to $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}$ as the twisted volume of the $(2,p)$ minimal string.
\end{prop}


\begin{rem}
The crucial difference between the combinatorial formulae of Theorem \ref{thm_combi_MV} and Proposition \ref{prop:minimal_combi} is the degree constraint in the sum. 
In the computation of the Masur-Veech volume, the imposed degree constraint is $|\mathbf{d}|=3g-3+n-k$. On the other hand for the $(2,p)$ minimal string, the weaker degree constraint $|\mathbf{d}|\le 3g-3+n-k$ is imposed.
If the degree constraint for the Masur-Veech volume is instead imposed for the volume formula of the minimal string, 
then the twisted volumes $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{g,n}$ reduce to the Masur-Veech volumes $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}_{g,n}$.
\end{rem}


Here we show combinatorial computations for $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{1,1}$ and $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{0,4}$.


\begin{ex}[$g=1, n=1$]
By the weaker constraint $|\mathbf{d}|\le 3g-3+n-k$ in the sum in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_minimal_volume}, 
an extra contribution to the sum in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_minimal_volume} is found for $k=0$. 
Namely for this contribution, there are no multicurves in $S_{1,1}$, and the factor $\prod_{i=1}^k(2d_i+1)!\zeta(2d_i+2)$ is absent. 
The corresponding stable graph $\Gamma_{1,1}^{(0)}$ has one vertex labeled by $g=1$ and one half-edge as described in Figure \ref{fig:stable_graph_minimal} (top).
\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{3.5cm}
\hspace*{-6cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=50mm]{multi_curve_minimal.pdf}
 \vspace{0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:stable_graph_minimal}
Top: A stable graph $\Gamma_{1,1}^{(0)}$ from $(S_{1,1},\emptyset)$.
Bottom: A stable graph $\Gamma_{0,4}^{(0)}$ from $(S_{0,4},\emptyset)$.
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
The polynomial factor obeys $(\emptyset)_{\Gamma_{1,1}^{(0)}}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}
=V^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{1,1}(0)=\pi^2s(1-1/p^2)/12$ for this stable graph, 
where we introduced the deformation parameter $s$ following Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen}.
The contributions to $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{1,1}$ from the stable graph $\Gamma_{1,1}^{(0)}$ is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:minimal_volume_11_2}
\frac{\alpha_{1,1}}{\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{1,1}^{(0)})\big|}\,
(\emptyset)_{\Gamma_{1,1}^{(0)}}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}\, \frac{1}{2!}
=\frac{2\pi^2s}{3}\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right).
\end{align}
Combining the contribution \eqref{MV_volume_11} from the stable graph $\Gamma_{1,1}^{(1)}$, one finds 
\begin{align}
\label{eq:minimal_volume_11}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{1,1}=\frac{2\pi^2s}{3}\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)+\frac{2\pi^2}{3}.
\end{align}
This agrees with 
$\beta_{1,1}V^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{1,1}[\sfm](0)=2^3\cdot \pi^2(s-s/p^2+1)/12$ in 
eq.\eqref{eq:minimal_twisted} 
(see Table \ref{lst_mst_twist_s} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}).
\end{ex}



\begin{ex}[$g=0, n=4$]
We compute an extra contribution of $k=0$ which comes 
from the weaker constraint $|\mathbf{d}|\le 3g-3+n-k$ in the sum in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_minimal_volume}.
The corresponding stable graph $\Gamma_{0,4}^{(0)}$ has one vertex labeled by $g=0$ and four half-edges as described in Figure \ref{fig:stable_graph_minimal} (bottom).
The polynomial factor obeys $(\emptyset)_{\Gamma_{0,4}^{(0)}}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}
=V^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{0,4}(0,0,0,0)=2\pi^2s(1-1/p^2)$
for this stable graph.
The contributions to $\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{0,4}$ from the stable graph $\Gamma_{0,4}^{(0)}$ is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:minimal_volume_04_2}
\frac{\alpha_{0,4}}{\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{0,4}^{(0)})\big|}\,
(\emptyset)_{\Gamma_{0,4}^{(0)}}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}\, \frac{1}{2!}
=8\pi^2s \left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right).
\end{align}
Combining the contribution \eqref{MV_volume_04} from the stable graph $\Gamma_{0,4}^{(1)}$, one finds 
\begin{align}
\label{eq:minimal_volume_04}
\mathrm{Vol}\mathcal{Q}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{0,4}=
8\pi^2s \left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)+2\pi^2.
\end{align}
This agrees with 
$\beta_{0,4}V^{\mathrm{M}(p)}_{0,4}[\sfm](0,0,0,0)=2^2\cdot \pi^2(4s-4s/p^2+1)/2$ in 
eq.\eqref{eq:minimal_twisted} 
(see Table \ref{lst_mst_twist_s} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}).
\end{ex}



\subsection{Generalizations of the combinatorial formula: supersymmetric models}\label{sec:combi_super}

The combinatorial formula in Theorem \ref{thm_combi_MV} is further generalized to the volume polynomials for the supersymmetric models
which is associated with the BGW tau function \cite{Alexandrov:2016kjl}.
We consider the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring whose volume polynomials interpolate
the volume polynomials $V^{\mathrm{B}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ for $p=1$ and the super Weil-Petersson volumes $V^{\mathrm{SWP}}_{g,n}(L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ for $p=\infty$, 
and find the following proposition.

\begin{prop}[Combinatorial formula for the twisted volume of $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstrings]\label{prop:minimal_super_combi} 
Let $\overline{G}_{g,n}$ be the set of stable graphs which does not contain any vertices associated to connected bordered Riemann surfaces of
genus zero.%
\footnote{
The volume polynomial $V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{0,n}(0,\ldots,0)$ is zero for any $n$.
}
The constant term in the twisted volume polynomial 
$V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ 
for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring 
is obtained, as a sum over the stable graphs $\Gamma\in \overline{G}_{g,n}$, by
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\label{eq:normalization_minimal_super_volume}
V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm](0,\cdots,0)
&=\sum_{\Gamma\in \overline{G}_{g,n}}
\frac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}\left(\Gamma\right)|}
\sum_{|\mathbf{d}|\le g-1-k}(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)_{\Gamma}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}
\\
&\hspace{12em}\times
\prod_{i=1}^k(2d_i+1)!\, \zeta(2d_i+2),
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $(2d_1,\ldots,2d_k)_{\Gamma}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}$ is
defined by eq.\eqref{vol_component_comb} from the twisted volume polynomial 
$V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]$.
\end{prop}


\begin{rem}\label{rem:super_minimal_volume}
If the degree constraint $|\mathbf{d}|\le g-1-k$ in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_minimal_super_volume} is replaced by the stronger condition $|\mathbf{d}|=g-1-k$,
then the  the twisted volume $V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{g,n}[\sfm](0,\cdots,0)$ for any odd $p$
reduces to $V^{\mathrm{B}}_{g,n}[\sfm](0,\cdots,0)$.
\end{rem}


Here we show combinatorial computations for $(g,n)=(2,1)$ and $(3,1)$.

\begin{ex}[$g=2, n=1$]
One finds three stable graphs which correspond to decompositions \eqref{eq:cut_Riemann_surface} of $S_{2,1}$ without $g=0$ components as described in Figure \ref{fig:stable_graph_super_21}.
\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{5cm}
\hspace*{-6cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=60mm]{multi_curve_super_21.pdf}
 \vspace{0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:stable_graph_super_21}
Stable graphs $\Gamma_{2,1}^{(0)},\Gamma_{2,1}^{(1)},\Gamma_{2,1}^{(2)}\in\overline{G}_{2,1}$ obtained from the 
decompositions of $S_{2,1}$ which do not involve $S_{0,n}$'s. 
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
For the graph $\Gamma_{2,1}^{(0)}$, a contribution 
in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_minimal_super_volume} is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:super_volume_21_0}
\mathrm{vol}^{(0)}_{2,1}=
\frac{1}{\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{2,1}^{(0)})\big|}\, 
(\emptyset)_{\Gamma^{(0)}_{2,1}}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}
=\frac{9\pi^2s}{64}\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right),
\end{align}
where $(\emptyset)_{\Gamma^{(0)}_{2,1}}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}=V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,1}(0)$, 
and the deformation parameter $s$ is introduced following Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen_super}.
For the graph $\Gamma_{2,1}^{(1)}$, a contribution 
in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_minimal_super_volume} is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:super_volume_21_1}
\mathrm{vol}^{(1)}_{2,1}=
\frac{1}{\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{2,1}^{(1)})\big|}\, 
(0)_{\Gamma^{(1)}_{2,1}}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}\, \zeta(2)
=\frac{\pi^2}{384},
\end{align}
where $(0)_{\Gamma^{(1)}_{2,1}}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}
=\textrm{the coefficient of $\ell^0$ in }
V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,2}(\ell,0)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,1}(\ell)=1/64$.
For the graph $\Gamma_{2,1}^{(2)}$, a contribution 
in eq.\eqref{eq:normalization_minimal_super_volume} is
\begin{align}
\label{eq:super_volume_21_2}
\mathrm{vol}^{(2)}_{2,1}=
\frac{1}{\big|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{2,1}^{(2)})\big|}\, (0)_{\Gamma^{(2)}_{2,1}}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}\, \zeta(2)
=\frac{\pi^2}{48},
\end{align}
where $(0)_{\Gamma^{(2)}_{2,1}}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}
=\textrm{the coefficient of $\ell^0$ in }
V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,3}(\ell,\ell,0)=1/4$ and $\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma_{2,1}^{(2)})=\mathbb{Z}/2\mathbb{Z}$.
Summing these three contributions, one obtains
\begin{align}
\label{super_volume_21}
&
V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,1}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](0)
=\mathrm{vol}^{(0)}_{2,1}+\mathrm{vol}^{(1)}_{2,1}+\mathrm{vol}^{(2)}_{2,1}
=\frac{\pi^2}{128}
\left(
18s\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)+3
\right),
\end{align}
which agrees with the constant term of the twisted volume polynomial obtained from the twisted ABO topological recursion
(see Table \ref{lst_super_mst_twist_s} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}).
\end{ex}



\begin{ex}[$g=3, n=1$]
One finds ten multicurves which decompose $S_{3,1}$ without $g=0$ components as described in Figure \ref{fig:stable_graph_super_31}.
\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{5.5cm}
\hspace*{-8cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=60mm]{multi_curve_super_31.pdf}
 \vspace{0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:stable_graph_super_31}
Ten Stable graphs obtained from the decompositions of $S_{3,1}$ which do not involve $S_{0,n}$'s. 
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}
Summing these ten contributions, one obtains
\begin{align}
\label{eq:super_volume_31}
&V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{3,1}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](0)
\\
&\nonumber
=V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{3,1}(0)
\\&\nonumber
\quad\;
+\left(
V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,1}(x)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,2}(x,0)
+V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,1}(x)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,2}(x,0)
+\frac{1}{2}V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,3}(x,x,0)
\right)\bigg|_{x^0}\zeta(2)
\\&\nonumber
\quad\;
+\left(
V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,1}(x)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,2}(x,0)
+V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,1}(x)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,2}(x,0)
+\frac{1}{2}V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{2,3}(x,x,0)
\right)\bigg|_{x^2}3!\zeta(4)
\\
\nonumber 
&\quad\;
+\biggl(
V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,1}(x)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,2}(x,y)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,2}(y,0)
+\frac{1}{2}V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,1}(x)V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,3}(x,y,0)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,1}(y)
\\
\nonumber 
&\quad\quad\quad
+\frac{1}{2}V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,2}(x,y)V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,3}(x,y,0)
+\frac{1}{2} V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,3}(x,y,y)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,2}(x,0)
\\
\nonumber 
&\quad\quad\quad
+\frac{1}{2}V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,1}(x)\cdot V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,4}(x,y,y,0)
+\frac{1}{2^3}V^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}_{1,5}(x,x,y,y,0)
\biggr)\bigg|_{x^0y^0}\zeta(2)^2
\nonumber \\
&=\frac{\pi^4}{1024}\left(
\left(1-\frac{1}{p^2}\right)
\left(6s^2\left(227-\frac{27}{p^2}\right)+255s\right)
+23\right),
\nonumber
\end{align}
where $|_{x^ky^l}$ picks up the coefficient of $x^ky^l$ in the polynomials.
This result agrees with the constant term of the twisted volume polynomial obtained from the twisted ABO topological recursion (see Table \ref{lst_super_mst_twist_s} of Appendix \ref{sec:table_vol_with_twist}).
\end{ex}





%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{CEO topological recursion}\label{sec:topological_recursion}

In this section, we apply the CEO topological recursion \cite{CE,EO2007}, which is a Laplace dual formulation of the ABO topological recursion,
to the 2D gravity models listed in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}. 
In particular, in Section \ref{sec:twisting_tr} we provide a direct proof of 
Theorem \ref{thm:Laplace_dual_GR} on the Laplace dual relation between 
the ABO topological recursion with the Masur-Veech type twist
and the CEO topological recursion with the Masur-Veech type twist for the $(2,p)$ minimal string and the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring.


\subsection{Formulation}\label{sec:def_tr}

We briefly review the formulation of the CEO topological recursion, and 
describe a Laplace dual relation with the ABO topological recursion.

\begin{Def}\label{def:sp_curve}
A \emph{spectral curve} $\cC=(\Sigma;\sfx,\sfy,B)$ consists of a Riemann surface $\Sigma$, meromorphic functions $\sfx, \sfy: \Sigma \to {\IC}$ such that the zeros of $d\sfx$ 
are different from the zeros of $d\sfy$, and a bidifferential $B$ on 
$\Sigma^{\otimes 2}$.
\end{Def}


\begin{Def}[CEO topological recursion \cite{EO2007}]\label{def:top_rec}
For a spectral curve $\cC=(\Sigma;\sfx,\sfy,B)$ such that the zeros of $d\sfx$ are simple, 
the meromorphic multidifferentials $\omega_{g,n}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)$, 
$z_i \in \Sigma$, labeled by $g \ge 0, n \ge 1$ satisfying $2g-2+n \ge 0$, 
are defined by the CEO topological recursion
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\omega_{g,n}(z_1, \ldots, z_n) &= 
\sum_{\alpha \in Ram}
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=\alpha}
K(z_1,w)\, \mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}(w, z_K),
\label{top_rec}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $K=\{2,\ldots,n\}$,
$Ram$ is the set of zeros of $d\sfx$, and
$K(z,w)$ is the \emph{recursion kernel} defined by
\begin{align}
K(z,w)=\frac{\int_{w}^{\overline{w}} B(\cdot, z)}
{2 \left(\sfy(w) d\sfx(w)-\sfy(\overline{w}) d\sfx(\overline{w})\right)},
\label{rec_kernel}
\end{align}
and
\begin{align}
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}(w, z_K)=
\omega_{g-1,n+1}(w, \overline{w}, z_K)
+ \mathop{\sum_{h+h'=g}}
\limits_{J \cup J'=K}^{\mathrm{no\, (0,1)}}
\omega_{h,1+|J|}(w, z_J)\, \omega_{h',1+|J'|}(\overline{w}, z_{J'}).
\label{rec_omega}
\end{align}
Here $\overline{w}$ is the conjugate point of $w$ near $\alpha \in Ram$, 
and the summation does not include $(g,n)=(0,1)$ part, and 
\begin{align}
\omega_{0,2}(z_1, z_2) = B(z_1, z_2),
\label{top_rec_ini}
\end{align}
and for $J=\{i_1, \ldots, i_{|J|}\} \subseteq K$, 
$z_J=\{z_{i_1}, \ldots, z_{i_{|J|}}\}$ and
$z_{J'}=\{z_{i_{|J|+1}}, \ldots, z_{i_{n-1}}\}$.
\end{Def}


In this paper, we focus on a class of spectral curves $\cC=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy,B)$ with coordinate functions
\begin{align}
\sfx=\sfx(z)=\frac12 z^2,
\qquad
\sfy=\sfy(z),
\qquad
z \in {\IP}^1,
\label{sp_curve}
\end{align}
which 
has a simple ramification point only at $z=0$ (the solution to $d\sfx(z)=0$).
$\sfy(z) \in {\IC}$ is a meromorphic function of $z$, 
and $\cC$ admits the global Galois covering by the conjugation $\overline{z}=-z$ and $(x(\overline{z}),y(\overline{z}))=(x(z),-y(z))$.
The bidifferential $B(z_1,z_2)$ has the double pole at the diagonal locus $z_1=z_2$ such that
\begin{align}
B(z_1, z_2)=\frac{dz_1 \otimes dz_2}{(z_1-z_2)^2},
\qquad
z_1, z_2 \in {\IP}^1.
\label{bergman}
\end{align}
For this class of spectral curves, 
$Ram=\{0\}$ owing to $\overline{w}=-w$ near $w=0$, and 
the recursion kernel for the CEO topological recursion is
\begin{align}
K(z,w)=\frac{\int_{w}^{-w} B(\cdot, z)}{2w\, (\sfy(w)-\sfy(-w))\, dw}=\frac{(-1)\, dz}{(z^2-w^2)\, (\sfy(w)-\sfy(-w))\, dw}.
\label{sym_diff_no_tw}
\end{align}
And we introduce correlation functions.
\begin{Def}\label{def:top_rec_correl}
The correlation functions $W_{g,n}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)$ for $2g-2+n \ge 0$ are defined by
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}(z_1, \ldots, z_n) \otimes_{i=1}^n dz_i =
\omega_{g,n}(z_1, \ldots, z_n).
\label{correl_tr}
\end{align}
\end{Def}


From the general argument in \cite{Andersen:2017vyk,Andersen_GR}, 
one finds the following claim.

\begin{thm}[Laplace transform of the volume polynomial \cite{Andersen:2017vyk,Andersen_GR}]\label{thm:laplace_abo_ceo}
For the physical 2D gravity models listed in Table \ref{tab:kernel}, 
the correlation functions $W_{g,n}$ for $2g-2+n > 0$ are related to the volume polynomials $\VO_{g,n}$ in Definition \ref{def:geom_rec} by a Laplace transform
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}(z_1, \ldots, z_n) =
\mathcal{L}\{\VO_{g,n}\}(z_1,\ldots,z_n),
\label{laplace}
\end{align}
where the operator $\mathcal{L}$ acts on a function $f(z_1,\ldots,z_n)$ as
\begin{align}
\mathcal{L}\{f\}(z_1,\ldots,z_n):=
\int_{\IR_+^n} f(L_1,\ldots,L_n)\, 
\e^{-\sum_{i=1}^n z_iL_i}\, \prod_{i=1}^n L_i dL_i.
\label{eq:Laplace}
\end{align}
In particular, for the expansion \eqref{gr_exp}, we find
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}(z_1, \ldots, z_n) =
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n \ge 0} F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\, 
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^{2a_i+2}}.
\label{laplace_exp}
\end{align}
\end{thm}


\begin{rem}
In Appendix \ref{sec:Derivation_Mirz}, 
based on the Laplace dual relation \eqref{laplace} 
we derive the kernel functions \eqref{eq:H_minimal} and \eqref{eq:H_super_minimal}, which are not known before in the literature, 
of the $(2,p)$ minimal string and the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring from 
the spectral curves in eqs.\eqref{sp_curve_mg} 
and \eqref{sp_curve_mg_super}.
Note that the ``local'' initial data $(\sfA^{a_1}_{a_2, a_3}, \sfB^{a_1}_{a_2, a_3}, \sfC^{a_1}_{a_2, a_3}, \sfD^{a_1})$ in eqs.\eqref{geom_rec_coeff} and \eqref{geom_rec_coeff_ini} are found in \cite{Andersen:2017vyk,Ooms:2019}.
\end{rem}

In Section \ref{sec:examples_tr_boson} and \ref{sec:examples_tr_super}, 
we will discuss the correlation functions defined by the CEO topological recursion for the physical 2D gravity models
and show some computational results of $W_{g,n}$ explicitly for our use in other sections and our checks of consistency of computations.


\subsection{Bosonic models}\label{sec:examples_tr_boson}

Here we consider the bosonic models in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}.

\subsubsection{Airy and KdV}\label{subsec:tr_kw}

For the Airy spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{A}},B)$ with 
coordinate functions
\begin{align}
\sfx(z)=\frac12 z^2,
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{A}}(z)=z,
\label{sp_curve_kw}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, 
the CEO topological recursion defines the meromorphic multidifferentials
\begin{align}
\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
K^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1,w)\, 
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{A}}(w, z_K)
=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
\otimes_{i=1}^n \frac{dz_i}{z_i^{2a_i+2}},
\label{airy_mdiff}
\end{align}
which give the Airy volume coefficients $F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in eq.\eqref{feg_kw}, where
\begin{align}
K^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1,w)=
\frac{(-1)\, dz_1}{2\left(z_1^2-w^2\right)wdw},
\label{rec_k_airy}
\end{align}
is the recursion kernel for $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}$. 
From eq.\eqref{airy_mdiff}, some of the correlation functions are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
W_{0,3}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1, z_2, z_3)=
\prod_{i=1}^3 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\quad
W_{1,1}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1)=
\frac{1}{8z_1^4},
\\
&
W_{0,4}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1, \cdots, z_4)=
\left(\sum_{i=1}^4 \frac{3}{z_i^2}\right)
\prod_{i=1}^4 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\quad
W_{1,2}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1, z_2)=
\left(
\sum_{i=1}^2 \frac{5}{8 z_i^4} 
+ \frac{3}{8 z_1^2 z_2^2}
\right)
\prod_{i=1}^2 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\\
&
W_{0,5}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1, \cdots, z_5)=
\left(
\sum_{i=1}^5 \frac{15}{z_i^4} 
+ \sum_{1\le i<j \le 5} \frac{18}{z_i^2 z_j^2}
\right)\prod_{i=1}^5 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\\
&
W_{1,3}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1, z_2, z_3)=
\left(
\sum_{i=1}^3 \frac{35}{8 z_i^6}
+ \sum_{1\le i,j \le 3} \frac{15}{4 z_i^2 z_j^4}
+ \frac{9}{4 z_1^2 z_2^2 z_3^2}
\right)
\prod_{i=1}^3 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\\
&
W_{2,1}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1)=
\frac{105}{128z_1^{10}}.
\label{airy_tr_ex}
\end{split}
\end{align}

We now introduce the KdV spectral curve which deforms 
the Airy spectral curve.

\begin{Def}[KdV spectral curve]\label{def:kdv}
The KdV spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{KdV}}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}},B)$ is defined by
\begin{align}
\sfx(z)=\frac12 z^2,
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z)=z + \sum_{a \ge 2}\sfu_{a}\, z^{a},
\label{sp_curve_kdv}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman},
where $\sfu_{a}$ are time variables. 
The KdV spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{KdV}}$ yields the Airy spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}$ when $\sfu_{a}=0$.
\end{Def}


The correlation functions
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{KdV}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\,
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^{2a_i+2}},
\label{kdv_mdiff}
\end{align}
obtained from the CEO topological recursion for $\cC^{\mathrm{KdV}}$ 
obey the following proposition \cite{Dunin-Barkowski:2012kbi}.

\begin{prop}[\cite{Dunin-Barkowski:2012kbi}]\label{prop:kdv}
The coefficients $F^{\mathrm{KdV}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in eq.\eqref{kdv_mdiff} are written in terms of 
the volume coefficients $F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in eq.\eqref{airy_mdiff}
(or eq.\eqref{feg_kw}) as
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{KdV}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}=
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}
\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 2} 
\left(\prod_{j=1}^m \frac{\sfu_{2b_j-1}}{2b_j+1}\right)
F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m},
\label{kdv_airy}
\end{align}
where the sum over $m$ and $b_j$ satisfies
\begin{align}
\sum_{i=1}^n a_i = 3g-3+n + m - \sum_{j=1}^m b_j,
\label{hom_kdv}
\end{align}
by the homogeneity condition \eqref{hom_kw} for the volume coefficients.
\end{prop}
\begin{proof}
The CEO topological recursion for the KdV spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{KdV}}$ gives
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)&=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
\frac{(-1)\, dz_1}{\left(z_1^2-w^2\right)
\left(\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w)-\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}}(-w)\right)dw}\,
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w, z_K)
\\
&=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
K^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1,w)\, 
Y^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w)\,
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w, z_K),
\label{kdv_ceo}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $K^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1,w)$ is the recursion kernel \eqref{rec_k_airy} for the Airy spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}$, and
\begin{align}
Y^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w)
=\frac{2w}{\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w)-\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}}(-w)}
=\sum_{m \ge 0} (-1)^m
\left(\sum_{b \ge 2}\sfu_{2b-1} w^{2b-2}\right)^m
=1 + \mathcal{O}(w^2),
\end{align}
is a regular even function of $w$ at $w=0$. 

A key formula to prove the proposition is \cite{Dunin-Barkowski:2012kbi},
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_1=0}
\frac{(-1)\, Y(w_1)\, R(w_1)}{2\left(w_0^2-w_1^2\right)w_1}
&=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_1=0}
\left(\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_2=w_1}
+\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_2=- w_1}\right)
\frac{(-1)\, dw_2}{2\left(w_0^2-w_2^2\right)w_2}\, 
\frac{w_2^2\, Y(w_2)\, R(w_1)}{\left(w_2^2-w_1^2\right)w_1}
\\
&=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_2=0}
\frac{w_2^2\, Y(w_2)dw_2}{\left(w_0^2-w_2^2\right)w_2}\,
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_1=0}
\frac{(-1)\, R(w_1)}{2\left(w_2^2-w_1^2\right)w_1},
\label{key_f}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $Y(w)$ is a regular function of $w$ at $w=0$ and 
$R(w)$ is a meromorphic differential of $w$.
Using this formula recursively, we rewrite eq.\eqref{kdv_ceo} as
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)&=
\sum_{m \ge 0}(-1)^m
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_m=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_m)\, dz_1}{\left(z_1^2-w_m^2\right)w_m}\,
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_{m-1}=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_{m-1})\, dw_m}{\left(w_m^2-w_{m-1}^2\right)w_{m-1}}
\\
&\qquad
\times \cdots \times
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_1=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_1)\, dw_2}{\left(w_2^2-w_1^2\right)w_1}\,
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
K^{\mathrm{A}}(w_1,w)\, 
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w, z_K),
\label{kdv_ceo_ind}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where
\begin{align}
\sfu(w)=
\sum_{b \ge 2}\sfu_{2b-1} w^{2b},
\end{align}
and the residue operators
\begin{align}
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_j=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_j)\, dw}{\left(w^2-w_j^2\right)w_j},
\label{dilaton_leaves_a}
\end{align}
acting on a meromorphic differential of $w_j$ is referred to as the \emph{Airy dilaton leaves}.
Therefore, the KdV meromorphic multidifferentials $\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}$ 
are regarded as 
the Airy meromorphic multidifferentials $\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{A}}$ 
decorated by the Airy dilaton leaves. 

To find such decorations,
we compare a meromorphic even differential 
$R(w)=\sum_{a} R_a dw/w^{2a}$ of $w$ 
decorated by an Airy dilaton leaf,
\begin{align}
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_j=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_j)\, dw\, R(w_j)}{\left(w^2-w_j^2\right)w_j}
=
\sum_{d \ge 0}\frac{dw}{w^{2d+2}}
\sum_{b \ge 2}\sfu_{2b-1}\, R_{d+b},
\label{kdv_decoration_1}
\end{align}
with the $(g,n)=(0,2)$ part in the CEO topological recursion for $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}$,
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_j=0}
K^{\mathrm{A}}(w,w_j)
\left(\frac{B(w_j,v)}{dv}\, R(-w_j)+\frac{B(-w_j,v)}{dv}\, R(w_j)\right)
\\
&=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_j=0}
\frac{R(w_j)\, dw}{2\left(w^2-w_j^2\right)w_j}
\left(\frac{1}{(v-w_j)^2}+\frac{1}{(v+w_j)^2}\right)
=
\sum_{d \ge 0}\frac{dw}{w^{2d+2}}
\sum_{b \ge 0} \frac{2b+1}{v^{2b+2}}\, R_{d+b}.
\label{kdv_decoration_2}
\end{split}
\end{align}
By this comparison, it is found that the decoration \eqref{kdv_decoration_1} of the Airy dilaton leaf is translated into a decorated $(g,n)=(0,2)$ part in the CEO topological recursion for $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}$.

In this translation, the Airy meromorphic differential acquires an extra marked point $v=1$,
and we find the sum in eq.\eqref{kdv_decoration_1} by replacing the sum in eq.\eqref{kdv_decoration_2} by a weighted sum such that
\begin{align}
\sum_{b \ge 0} \frac{2b+1}{v^{2b+2}}\, R_{d+b}
\;\to\;
\sum_{b \ge 0} \frac{2b+1}{v^{2b+2}}\, \mathsf{wt}_{b}(\sfu)\, R_{d+b}
=
\sum_{b \ge 2}\sfu_{2b-1}\, R_{d+b},
\end{align}
with weight factors
\begin{align}
\mathsf{wt}_{b}(\sfu)=
\begin{cases}
0 \quad 
& \textrm{for}\ b = 0,1,
\\
\frac{\sfu_{2b-1}}{2b+1} \quad 
& \textrm{for}\ b \ge 2.
\label{dilaton_leaf_eff}
\end{cases}
\end{align}
In the following, we refer to this translation for the Airy dilaton leaf which decorates the $(g,n)=(0,2)$ part in the multidifferential
 as the \emph{Airy translation}. 
 In the following discussions,
 we adopt the Airy translation to prove the formula \eqref{kdv_airy}  by the mathematical induction on $2g-2+n \ge 1$. 

For $(g,n)=(0,3)$, eq.\eqref{kdv_ceo_ind} gives
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\omega_{0,3}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z_1, z_2, z_3)&=
\sum_{m \ge 0}(-1)^m
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_m=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_m)\, dz_1}{\left(z_1^2-w_m^2\right)w_m} \cdots
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_1=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_1)\, dw_2}{\left(w_2^2-w_1^2\right)w_1}\,
\omega_{0,3}^{\mathrm{A}}(w_1, z_2, z_3)
\\
&=
\omega_{0,3}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1, z_2, z_3),
\label{kdv_ceo_step1}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where the Airy dilaton leaves do not contribute in this case.
For $(g,n)=(1,1)$, eq.\eqref{kdv_ceo_ind} gives
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\omega_{1,1}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z_1)&=
\sum_{m \ge 0}(-1)^m
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_m=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_m)\, dz_1}{\left(z_1^2-w_m^2\right)w_m} \cdots
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_1=0}
\frac{\sfu(w_1)\, dw_2}{\left(w_2^2-w_1^2\right)w_1}\,
\omega_{1,1}^{\mathrm{A}}(w_1)
\\
&=
\omega_{1,1}^{\mathrm{A}}(z_1)+
\sum_{a_1 \ge 0, b_1 \ge 2}
\frac{\sfu_{2b_1-1}}{2b_1+1}\,
F^{\mathrm{A}(1)}_{a_1,b_1}\, \frac{dz_1}{z_1^{2a_1+2}},
\label{kdv_ceo_step1_2}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where only one Airy dilaton leaf contributes and the Airy translation is adopted.
Thus, the equations \eqref{kdv_airy} for $(g,n)=(0,3), (1,1)$ are obtained.


Next, under the assumption that the formula \eqref{kdv_airy} is correct for any $(g,n)$ with 
$2g-2+n \le k$, 
we consider eq.\eqref{kdv_ceo_ind} for $(g,n)$ with $2g-2+n=k+1$. 
The coefficients of $\otimes_{i=2}^n dz_i/z_i^{2a_i+2}$ 
in the factor $\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(w, z_K)$ in 
eq.\eqref{kdv_ceo_ind} are rewritten 
under this assumption as
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\sum_{a, b \ge 0}
\frac{(-1)\, dw \otimes dw}{w^{2a+2b+4}}
\Bigg(F^{\mathrm{KdV}(g-1)}_{a,b,a_2,\ldots,a_n}
+
\mathop{\sum_{h+h'=g}'}
\limits_{J \subseteq K}
F^{\mathrm{KdV}\, (h)}_{a,a_{i_1},\ldots,a_{i_{|J|}}}
F^{\mathrm{KdV}\, (h')}_{b,a_{i_{|J|+1}},\ldots,a_{i_{n-1}}}\Bigg)
\\
&=
\sum_{a, b \ge 0}
\frac{(-1)\, dw \otimes dw}{w^{2a+2b+4}}
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 2}
\Bigg(\prod_{j=1}^m\mathsf{wt}_{b_j}(\sfu)\Bigg)
\\
&\
\times
\Bigg(F^{\mathrm{A}(g-1)}_{a,b,a_2,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m}
+
\mathop{\sum_{h+h'=g}'}
\limits_{J \subseteq K}
\sum_{\ell=0}^m
\binom{m}{\ell}
F^{\mathrm{A}\, (h)}_{a,a_{i_1},\ldots,a_{i_{|J|}}, b_1, \ldots, b_{\ell}}
F^{\mathrm{A}\, (h')}_{b,a_{i_{|J|+1}},\ldots,a_{i_{n-1}}, b_{\ell+1}, \ldots, b_m}\Bigg),
\label{kdv_airy_step2}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where the sum $\sum_{h+h'=g}'$ does not include 
$(h, J)=(0,\emptyset)$, $(g,K)$.
The symmetric factor $m!$ for the insertion of $m$ Airy dilaton leaves arises, since extra marked points at $v=1$ are indistinguishable.

Plugging eq.\eqref{kdv_airy_step2} into the right hand side of eq.\eqref{kdv_ceo_ind}, we see that the Airy dilaton leaves in eq.\eqref{kdv_ceo_ind} compensate 
the $(h, h', J)=(0,g,\emptyset)$, $(g,0,K)$ parts in 
eq.\eqref{kdv_airy_step2} by the Airy translations.
As a result, we obtain
\begin{align}
\label{KdV_leave}
\begin{split}
&
\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)
\\
&
=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} \otimes_{i=1}^n \frac{dz_i}{z_i^{2a_i+2}}\,
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 2}
\Bigg(\prod_{j=1}^m\mathsf{wt}_{b_j}(\sfu)\Bigg)
\\
&\
\times
\Bigg(F^{\mathrm{A}(g-1)}_{a,b,a_2,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m}
+
\sum_{\substack{h+h'=g\\ J \subseteq K\\ 0 \le \ell \le m}}''
\binom{m}{\ell}
F^{\mathrm{A}\, (h)}_{a,a_{i_1},\ldots,a_{i_{|J|}}, b_1, \ldots, b_{\ell}}
F^{\mathrm{A}\, (h')}_{b,a_{i_{|J|+1}},\ldots,a_{i_{n-1}}, b_{\ell+1}, \ldots, b_m}\Bigg)
\\
&
=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} \otimes_{i=1}^n \frac{dz_i}{z_i^{2a_i+2}}\,
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 2}
\Bigg(\prod_{j=1}^m \frac{\sfu_{2b_j-1}}{2b_j+1}\Bigg)
F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m},
\end{split}
\end{align}
where the sum $\sum_{h+h'=g}''$ does not include 
$(h, J, \ell)=(0,\emptyset, 0)$, $(g,K, m)$. 
Thus, the induction is completed and the claim is proved.
\end{proof}





\subsubsection{Weil-Petersson volumes}\label{subsec:tr_mir}

For the Weil-Petersson spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{WP}}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{WP}},B)$ 
defined by \cite{Eynard:2007fi},
\begin{align}
\sfx(z)=\frac12 z^2,
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)=\frac{1}{2\pi} \sin(2\pi z)
= \sum_{a \ge 1} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{a-1}}{(2a-1)!!\, (a-1)!}\, z^{2a-1},
\label{sp_curve_mir}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, 
the CEO topological recursion computes 
the Weil-Petersson volume coefficients \eqref{feg_mir}, 
which give the Weil-Petersson volumes $\VO_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}$ in eq.\eqref{mir_volume}, by 
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}^{\mathrm{WP}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{WP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\,
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^{2a_i+2}}.
\label{wp_mdiff}
\end{align}
The coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mir} is 
found from a specialization%
\footnote{
This specialization is also found in the physics literatures \cite{Dijkgraaf:2018vnm,Okuyama:2019xbv}.
}
of the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_kdv} of the KdV spectral curve as 
\begin{align}
\sfu_{2a}=0,\qquad
\sfu_{2a+1}=\frac{(-2\pi^2)^a}{(2a+1)!!\, a!},
\label{sp_kdv_wp}
\end{align}
and Proposition \ref{prop:kdv} implies a formula:
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{WP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}=
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}
\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 2} 
\left(\prod_{j=1}^m \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b_j-1}}{(2b_j+1)!!\, (b_j-1)!}\right)
F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m},
\label{wp_airy}
\end{align}
with the condition \eqref{hom_kdv}.



\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_tr_wp}
The deformation parameter $s$ in Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa} 
is implemented to the spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{WP}}$ by 
the replacement $\pi \to \pi \sqrt{s}$ for the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mir}.
\end{rem}




\subsubsection{$(2,p)$ minimal string}\label{subsec:tr_mg}

The spectral curve for the $(2,p)$ minimal string is found from the disk partition function with the FZZT boundary condition \cite{Fateev:2000ik,Teschner:2000md}.
For an positive odd integer $p$, 
the $(2,p)$ minimal string spectral curve 
$\cC^{\mathrm{M}(p)}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)},B)$ is defined by
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\sfx(z)&=\frac12 z^2,
\\
\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)&= \frac{(-1)^{\frac{p-1}{2}}}{2\pi} T_p\biggl(\frac{2\pi}{p}z\biggr)
=\frac{1}{2\pi} \sin\left(\frac{p}{2} \arccos\left(1-\frac{8\pi^2z^2}{p^2}\right)\right)
\\
&= \sum_{a=1}^{\frac{p+1}{2}} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{a-1}}{(2a-1)!!\, (a-1)!}
\prod_{i=1}^{a-1}\left(1-\frac{(2i-1)^2}{p^2}\right) z^{2a-1},
\label{sp_curve_mg}
\end{split}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, 
where $T_p(z)$ denotes the Chebyshev polynomial of the first kind defined by
\begin{align}
T_p(\cos \theta)=\cos(p\, \theta).
\label{chebyshev_first}
\end{align}
The minimal string spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{M}(p)}$ 
interpolates the Airy spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}$ and 
the Weil-Petersson spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{WP}}$ by
\begin{align}
\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(1)} (z) = \sfy^{\mathrm{A}}(z)\ 
\textrm{in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_kw}},
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(\infty)}(z) = \sfy^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)\ 
\textrm{in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mir}}.
\end{align}
The coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mg} is 
found from a specialization of the coordinate function 
$\sfy^{\mathrm{KdV}(p)}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_kdv} of the KdV spectral curve as
\begin{align}
\begin{cases}
\sfu_{2a}=0\
& \textrm{for}\ a \ge 1,
\\
\sfu_{2a+1}=
\frac{(-2\pi^2)^a}{(2a+1)!!\, a!}
\prod_{i=1}^{a}\left(1-\frac{(2i-1)^2}{p^2}\right)\ 
& \textrm{for}\ 1 \le a \le \frac{p-1}{2},
\\
\sfu_{2a+1}=0\
& \textrm{for}\ a \ge \frac{p+1}{2}.
\label{sp_kdv_ms}
\end{cases}
\end{align}
Proposition \ref{prop:kdv} then implies that 
$(2,p)$ minimal string volume coefficients 
$F^{\mathrm{M}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ of eq.\eqref{gr_exp_mg} in the correlation functions
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{M}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\,
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^{2a_i+2}},
\label{mst_mdiff}
\end{align}
obey a formula:
\begin{align}
\label{mst_airy}
&
F^{\mathrm{M}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
\\
&=
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}
\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 2} 
\left(\prod_{j=1}^m 
\frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b_j-1}}{(2b_j+1)!!\, (b_j-1)!}
\prod_{i=1}^{b_j-1}\left(1-\frac{(2i-1)^2}{p^2}\right)
\right)
F^{\mathrm{A}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m},
\nonumber
\end{align}
with the condition \eqref{hom_kdv}.

\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_tr_ms}
We can introduce the deformation parameter $s$ in Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen} by 
the replacement $\pi \to \pi \sqrt{s}$ for the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mg}.
\end{rem}


\subsection{Supersymmetric models}\label{sec:examples_tr_super}

Here we consider the supersymmetric models in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}.

\subsubsection{Bessel and BGW}\label{subsec:tr_be}

For the Bessel spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{B}}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{B}},B)$ with coordinate functions \cite{Do:2016odu},
\begin{align}
\sfx(z)=\frac12 z^2,
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{B}}(z)=\frac{1}{z},
\label{sp_curve_be}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, 
the CEO topological recursion defines the meromorphic multidifferentials
\begin{align}
\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
K^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,w)\,
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{B}}(w, z_K)=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{B}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
\otimes_{i=1}^n \frac{dz_i}{z_i^{2a_i+2}},
\label{bessel_mdiff}
\end{align}
and the Bessel volume coefficients $F^{\mathrm{B}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in 
eq.\eqref{feg_be} are obtained, 
where
\begin{align}
K^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,w)=
\frac{(-1)\, w\, dz_1}{2\left(z_1^2-w^2\right)dw},
\label{rec_k_bessel}
\end{align}
is the recursion kernel for the CEO topological recursion on the Bessel spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{B}}$.
Here, note the relation $\sfy^{\mathrm{B}}(z)=\partial_{\sfx} \sfy^{\mathrm{A}}(z)$ 
with the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{A}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_kw} of 
the Airy spectral curve. 
From eq.\eqref{bessel_mdiff}, some of the correlation functions are
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
W_{0,n}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1, \cdots, z_n)=0,
\quad
W_{1,n}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1, \cdots, z_n)=
\frac{(n-1)!}{8}
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\\
&
W_{2,1}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1)=
\frac{9}{128 z_1^4},
\quad
W_{2,2}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,z_2)=
\left(
\sum_{i=1}^2 \frac{27}{128 z_i^2}
\right)
\prod_{i=1}^2 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\\
&
W_{2,3}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,z_2,z_3)=
\left(
\sum_{i=1}^3 \frac{27}{32 z_i^2}
\right)
\prod_{i=1}^3 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\quad
W_{3,1}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1)=
\frac{225}{1024 z_1^6},
\\
&
W_{2,4}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,\cdots,z_4)=
\left(
\sum_{i=1}^4 \frac{135}{32 z_i^2}
\right)
\prod_{i=1}^4 \frac{1}{z_i^2},
\\
&
W_{3,2}^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,z_2)=
\left(
\sum_{i=1}^2 \frac{1125}{1024 z_i^4}
+ \frac{567}{512 z_1^2 z_2^2}
\right)
\prod_{i=1}^2 \frac{1}{z_i^2}.
\label{bessel_tr_ex}
\end{split}
\end{align}


Let us introduce the BGW spectral curve which deforms the Bessel spectral curve.

\begin{Def}[BGW spectral curve]\label{def:bgw}
The BGW spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{BGW}}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}},B)$ is 
defined by
\begin{align}
\sfx(z)=\frac12 z^2,
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}}(z)= \frac{1}{z} + \sum_{a \ge 0}\sfv_{a}\, z^{a},
\label{sp_curve_bgw}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, 
where $\sfv_{a}$ are time variables.
The BGW spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{BGW}}$ for $\sfv_{a}=0$ yields the Bessel spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{B}}$.
\end{Def}

Similar to Proposition \ref{prop:kdv}, the correlation functions
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}^{\mathrm{BGW}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{BGW}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\,
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^{2a_i+2}},
\label{bgw_mdiff}
\end{align}
obtained from the CEO topological recursion for $\cC^{\mathrm{BGW}}$ 
obey the following proposition.

\begin{prop}\label{prop:bgw}
The coefficients $F^{\mathrm{BGW}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in eq.\eqref{bgw_mdiff} are written in terms of 
the volume coefficients $F^{\mathrm{B}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in eq.\eqref{bessel_mdiff} (or eq.\eqref{feg_be})  as
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{BGW}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}=
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}
\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 1} 
\left(\prod_{j=1}^m \frac{\sfv_{2b_j-1}}{2b_j+1}\right)
F^{\mathrm{B}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m},
\label{bgw_bessel}
\end{align}
where the sum over $m$ and $b_j$ satisfies
\begin{align}
\sum_{i=1}^n a_i = g-1 - \sum_{j=1}^m b_j,
\label{hom_bgw}
\end{align}
by the homogeneity condition \eqref{hom_be}.
\end{prop}
\begin{proof}
The statement can shown in the parallel way as the proof of Proposition \ref{prop:kdv}. 
The CEO topological recursion for the BGW spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{BGW}}$ gives
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{BGW}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)&=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
\frac{(-1)\, dz_1}{\left(z_1^2-w^2\right)
\left(\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}}(w)-\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}}(-w)\right)dw}\,
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{BGW}}(w, z_K)
\\
&=
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
K^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,w)\,
Y^{\mathrm{BGW}}(w)\,
\mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{BGW}}(w, z_K),
\label{bgw_ceo}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $K^{\mathrm{B}}(z_1,w)$ is the recursion kernel \eqref{rec_k_bessel} 
for the Bessel spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{B}}$, and
\begin{align}
Y^{\mathrm{BGW}}(w)
=\frac{2}{w \left(\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}}(w)-\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}}(-w)\right)}
=\sum_{m \ge 0} (-1)^m
\left(\sum_{b \ge 1}\sfv_{2b-1} w^{2b}\right)^m
=1 + \mathcal{O}(w^2),
\end{align}
is a regular even function of $w$ around $w=0$. 
Using the formula \eqref{key_f} recursively, we rewrite eq.\eqref{bgw_ceo} as
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{BGW}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)&=
\sum_{m \ge 0}(-1)^m
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_m=0}
\frac{\sfv(w_m)\, w_m\, dz_1}{\left(z_1^2-w_m^2\right)}\,
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_{m-1}=0}
\frac{\sfv(w_{m-1})\, w_{m-1}\, dw_m}{\left(w_m^2-w_{m-1}^2\right)}
\\
&\qquad
\times \cdots \times
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_1=0}
\frac{\sfv(w_1)\, w_1\, dw_2}{\left(w_2^2-w_1^2\right)}\,
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w=0}
K^{\mathrm{B}}(w_1,w)\, \mathcal{R}\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{BGW}}(w, z_K),
\label{bgw_ceo_ind}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where
\begin{align}
\sfv(w)=
\sum_{b \ge 1}\sfv_{2b-1} w^{2b},
\end{align}
and the residue operators
\begin{align}
\mathop{\mathrm{Res}}\limits_{w_j=0}
\frac{\sfv(w_j)\, w_j\, dw}{\left(w^2-w_j^2\right)},
\label{dilaton_leaves_bgw}
\end{align}
acting on a meromorphic differential of $w_j$ are 
referred to as the \emph{Bessel dilaton leaves}.
In such a way, the BGW meromorphic multidifferentials $\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{BGW}}$ 
are obtained as 
the Bessel meromorphic multidifferentials $\omega_{g,n}^{\mathrm{B}}$ 
decorated by the Bessel dilaton leaves. 
Just like the Airy translation of the Airy dilaton leaf which decorates $(g,n)=(0,2)$ part in 
the CEO topological recursion for $\cC^{\mathrm{A}}$ with weights \eqref{dilaton_leaf_eff}, 
a Bessel dilaton leaf is translated into a decoration of the $(g,n)=(0,2)$ part in 
the CEO topological recursion for $\cC^{\mathrm{B}}$ with weights
\begin{align}
\begin{cases}
0 \quad 
& \textrm{for}\ b = 0,
\\
\frac{\sfv_{2b-1}}{2b+1} \quad 
& \textrm{for}\ b \ge 1.
\label{dilaton_leaf_eff_bgw}
\end{cases}
\end{align}
Repeating the same analysis as the proof of Proposition \ref{prop:kdv}, 
we find that eq.\eqref{bgw_bessel} holds.
\end{proof}



\subsubsection{Super Weil-Petersson volumes}\label{subsec:tr_sw}


For the super Weil-Petersson spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{SWP}}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{SWP}},B)$ 
defined by \cite{Stanford:2019vob,Norbury:2020vyi},
\begin{align}
\sfx(z)=\frac12 z^2,
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{SWP}}(z)=\frac{1}{z} \cos(2\pi z)
= \sum_{a \ge 0} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{a}}{(2a-1)!!\, a!}\, z^{2a-1},
\label{sp_curve_sw}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, 
the CEO topological recursion computes the super Weil-Petersson volume coefficients \eqref{feg_sw}, which give the super Weil-Petersson volumes, by 
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SWP}}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{SWP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\,
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^{2a_i+2}}.
\label{super_wp_mdiff}
\end{align}
Here, note the relation $\sfy^{\mathrm{SWP}}(z)=\partial_{\sfx} \sfy^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)$ 
with the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mir} of the Weil-Petersson spectral curve.
The coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{SWP}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_sw} is found from a specialization of 
the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_bgw} of the BGW spectral curve as
\begin{align}
\sfv_{2a}=0,\qquad
\sfv_{2a+1}=
\frac{(-2\pi^2)^{a+1}}{(2a+1)!!\, (a+1)!},
\label{sp_bgw_swp}
\end{align}
and Proposition \ref{prop:bgw} implies a formula:
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{SWP}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}=
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}
\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 1} 
\left(\prod_{j=1}^m 
\frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b_j}}{(2b_j+1)!!\, b_j!}\right)
F^{\mathrm{B}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m},
\label{swp_bessel}
\end{align}
with the condition \eqref{hom_bgw}.

\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_tr_wp_super}
The replacement $\pi \to \pi \sqrt{s}$ for the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{WP}}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_sw} introduces 
the deformation parameter $s$ in Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa_super}.
\end{rem}


\subsubsection{$(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring}\label{subsec:tr_mg_super}

The spectral curve 
$\cC^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}=({\IP}^1;\sfx,\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)},B)$ 
for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring
with the positive odd integer $p$, which is heuristically introduced by 
$\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z)=\partial_{\sfx} \sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)$ 
from the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)$ 
in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mg} of the $(2,p)$ minimal string spectral curve 
(see Appendix \ref{sec:type0A}), consists of
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\sfx(z)&=\frac12 z^2,
\\
\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z)&= \frac{(-1)^{\frac{p-1}{2}}}{z} U_{p-1}\biggl(\frac{2\pi}{p}z\biggr)
=\frac{4\pi}{p \sqrt{1-\left(1-\frac{8\pi^2z^2}{p^2}\right)^2}} 
\cos\left(\frac{p}{2} \arccos\left(1-\frac{8\pi^2z^2}{p^2}\right)\right)
\\
&= \sum_{a=0}^{\frac{p-1}{2}} \frac{(-2\pi^2)^{a}}{(2a-1)!!\, a!}
\prod_{i=1}^{a}\left(1-\frac{(2i-1)^2}{p^2}\right) z^{2a-1},
\label{sp_curve_mg_super}
\end{split}
\end{align}
and the bidifferential $B$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, 
where $U_p(z)$ is the Chebyshev polynomial of the second kind defined by
\begin{align}
U_{p-1}(\cos \theta)=\frac{\sin (p\, \theta)}{\sin \theta}.
\label{chebyshev_sec}
\end{align}
Notice that the spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}$ 
interpolates the Bessel spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{B}}$ and 
the super Weil-Petersson spectral curve $\cC^{\mathrm{SWP}}$ by
\begin{align}
\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(1)}(z) = \sfy^{\mathrm{B}}(z)\ 
\textrm{in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_be}},
\qquad
\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(\infty)}(z) = \sfy^{\mathrm{SWP}}(z)\ 
\textrm{in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_sw}}.
\end{align}
The coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mg_super} is found from 
a specialization of the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{BGW}(p)}(z)$ in 
eq.\eqref{sp_curve_bgw} of the BGW spectral curve as
\begin{align}
\begin{cases}
\sfv_{2a}=0\
& \textrm{for}\ a \ge 0,
\\
\sfv_{2a+1}=
\frac{(-2\pi^2)^{a+1}}{(2a+1)!!\, (a+1)!}
\prod_{i=1}^{a+1}\left(1-\frac{(2i-1)^2}{p^2}\right)\ 
& \textrm{for}\ 0 \le a \le \frac{p-3}{2},
\\
\sfv_{2a+1}=0\
& \textrm{for}\ a \ge \frac{p-1}{2}.
\label{sp_bgw_ms_super}
\end{cases}
\end{align}
Adopting this specialization to Proposition \ref{prop:bgw}, we find that 
the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring volume coefficients 
$F^{\mathrm{SM}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in the correlation functions
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z_1, \ldots, z_n)=
\sum_{a_1, \ldots, a_n \ge 0} F^{\mathrm{SM}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\,
\prod_{i=1}^n \frac{1}{z_i^{2a_i+2}},
\label{super_mst_mdiff}
\end{align}
obey a formula:
\begin{align}
F^{\mathrm{SM}(p)\, (g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}=
\sum_{m \ge 0}\frac{(-1)^m}{m!}
\sum_{b_1,\ldots,b_m \ge 1}
\left(
\prod_{j=1}^m 
\frac{(-2\pi^2)^{b_j}}{(2b_j+1)!!\, b_j!}
\prod_{i=1}^{b_j}\left(1-\frac{(2i-1)^2}{p^2}\right)
\right)
F^{\mathrm{B}(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n, b_1, \ldots, b_m},
\label{msst_bessel}
\end{align}
with the condition \eqref{hom_bgw}.


\begin{rem}\label{rem:fugacity_tr_ms_super}
The deformation parameter $s$ in Remark \ref{rem:fugacity_kappa_gen_super} 
is introduced by
the replacement $\pi \to \pi \sqrt{s}$ for the coordinate function $\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z)$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve_mg_super}.
\end{rem}



\subsection{CEO topological recursion with twist}\label{sec:twisting_tr}

\begin{Def}\label{def:sp_curve_tw}
We refer to a \emph{twisted spectral curve} $\cC[\sff]=(\Sigma;\sfx,\sfy,B[\sff])$ 
as a spectral curve with a twisted bidifferential $B[\sff]$ on $C^{\otimes 2}$ with the admissible test function $\sff:\mathbb{R}_+\to\mathbb{C}$.
\end{Def}


The twisted volume polynomial $V_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ with
an admissible test function $\mathsf{f}$ is equivalent to 
the multidifferential $\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)$ 
which satisfies the CEO topological recursion
for a twisted spectral curve \cite{Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV}.
These are related by the Laplace transform involving the action of 
\emph{twist-elimination} explained below.

In this article, we focus on the 2D gravity models listed in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}, but here we introduce 
several basic notions associated with the CEO topological recursion in a little general framework
to give a definition of the action of the twist-elimination map on the twisted multidifferential $\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)$
simply.
Here we consider a spectral curve $\cC=(\Sigma;\sfx,\sfy,B)$ such that 
the zeros of $d\sfx$ are simple, and a local coordinate $p$ near 
a branch point $\alpha$ obeys $\sfx=p^2/2+\sfx(\alpha)$.
For this set-up, we introduce a globally defined 1-form $\xi_a(z)$ on the spectral curve $\cC$ with $a \in \mathbb{Z}_{\ge 0}$ by%
\footnote{
For a spectral curve with the coordinate function $\sfx=z^2/2$, 
$z \in \IP^1$ in eq.\eqref{sp_curve} and 
the bidifferential $B(z, w)=dz \otimes dw/(z-w)^2$, $z, w \in \IP^1$ in eq.\eqref{bergman}, $\xi_a(z)=dz/z^{2a+2}$.
}
\begin{align}
\xi_a(z)=\underset{w=\alpha}{\mathrm{Res}}\;
\frac{dp(w)}{p(w)^{2a+2}}
\left(
\int_{\alpha}^w B(\cdot,z)
\right).
\label{eq:global_1-form}
\end{align}
The solutions $\omega_{g,n}(z_1,\ldots,z_n)$ $(2g-2+n \ge 1)$ of the CEO topological recursion are represented by the 1-forms $\xi_{a_i}(z_i)$ 
($i=1,\ldots,n$) as the basis of the multidifferentials:
\begin{align}
\omega_{g,n}(z_1,\ldots,z_n)=
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n\ge 0}
F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n} \otimes_{i=1}^n \xi_{a_i}(z_i).
\label{eq:expansion_multidifferential}
\end{align}
For a twisted spectral curve $\cC=(\Sigma;\sfx,\sfy,B[\sff])$, 
the solutions $\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)$ of 
the CEO topological recursion are also given on basis of
\begin{align}
\xi_a[\mathsf{f}](z)=
\underset{w=\alpha}{\mathrm{Res}}\;\frac{dp(w)}{p(w)^{2a+2}}
\left(
\int_{\alpha}^w B[\sff](\cdot,z)
\right),
\label{eq:twisted_1-form}
\end{align}
by
\begin{align}
\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)=
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n\ge 0}
F^{(g)}[\mathsf{f}]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n} \otimes_{i=1}^n\xi_{a_i}[\mathsf{f}](z_i).
\label{eq:twisted_multidifferential}
\end{align}


Now we introduce the twisted correlation function and the twist-elimination map below.

\begin{Def}\label{def:top_rec_correl_tw}
The twisted correlation functions $W_{g,n}[\sff](z_1, \ldots, z_n)$ for $2g-2+n \ge 0$ are defined by
\begin{align}
W_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n) \otimes_{i=1}^n dz_i =
\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n),
\label{eq:TR_corrleator}
\end{align}
and the  twisted kernel function $K[\mathsf{f}]$ is defined by
\begin{align}
K[\mathsf{f}](z,w)=\frac{\int_{w}^{\overline{w}} B[\sff](\cdot, z)}
{2 \left(\sfy(w) d\sfx(w)-\sfy(\overline{w}) d\sfx(\overline{w})\right)}.
\label{eq:twisted_kernel}
\end{align}
\end{Def}


\begin{Def}[Twist-elimination map]\label{def:twist_elimination}
Let $\Omega(\mathcal{C})$ be the space of meromorphic multidifferentials on a twisted spectral curve $\cC=(\Sigma;\sfx,\sfy,B[\sff])$, spanned by the symmetric tensors of the basis $\xi_a[\mathsf{f}](z_a)$ ($a=1,\ldots,n$). The \emph{twist-elimination map} $\mathcal{E}[z_I]$ with a set $I$ is a map on $\Omega(\mathcal{C})$ of which action replaces the basis $\xi_a[\mathsf{f}]$ by $\xi_{a}$ for $a\in I\cap\{1,\ldots,n\}$.
\end{Def}

From the above definition, we find the following three properties for the action of  the twist-elimination map:\\
1. For a sum of multidifferentials $\omega^{(1)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}],\omega^{(2)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}]\in \Omega(\mathcal{C})$,
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\label{eq:property1_elim}
&\mathcal{E}[z_I]\left(\omega^{(1)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)+\omega^{(2)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)\right)
\\
&=\mathcal{E}[z_I]\left(\omega^{(1)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)\right)+
\mathcal{E}[z_{I}]\left(\omega^{(2)}_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)\right).
\end{split}
\end{align}
2. For a tensor product of multidifferentials $\omega_{g_1,n_1}[\mathsf{f}],\omega_{g_2,n_2}[\mathsf{f}]\in \Omega(\mathcal{C})$,
\begin{align}
\label{eq:property2_elim}
&\mathcal{E}[z_I]\left(\omega_{g_1,n_1}[\mathsf{f}](z_{I_1})\otimes\omega_{g_2,n_2}[\mathsf{f}](z_{I_2})\right)
=\mathcal{E}[z_I]\left(\omega_{g_1,n_1}[\mathsf{f}](z_{I_1})\right)\otimes
\mathcal{E}[z_{I}]\left(\omega_{g_2,n_2}[\mathsf{f}](z_{I_2})\right),
\end{align}
where $I_1\cap I_2=\emptyset$.

\noindent{3.} For the twisted kernel \eqref{eq:twisted_kernel},
\begin{align}
&\cE[z]\{K[\mathsf{f}]\}(z,w)=K(z,w).
\label{eq:elim_kernel}
\end{align}


The action of the twist-elimination map $\mathcal{E}[z_I]$
on the twisted correlation function \eqref{eq:TR_corrleator} is induced by 
\begin{align}
\mathcal{E}[z_I]\left(\omega_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)\right)
=\mathcal{E}[z_{I}]
\left\{W_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}]\right\}(z_1,\ldots,z_n) \otimes_{i=1}^n dz_i.
\end{align}
For the case $I=\{i_1,\ldots,i_{\ell}\}\subseteq\{1,\ldots,n\}$,
we obtain partially untwisted correlation functions 
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\mathcal{E}[z_{i_1},\ldots,z_{i_\ell}]
\left\{W_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}]\right\}(z_1,\ldots,z_n) \otimes_{i=1}^n dz_i 
\\
&=
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n\ge 0}
F^{(g)}[\mathsf{f}]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
\otimes_{m=1}^{\ell} \xi_{a_{i_m}}(z_{i_m})\,
\otimes_{k \in\{1,\ldots,n\}\setminus \{i_1,\ldots,i_{\ell}\}}
\xi_{a_k}[\sff](z_k).
\label{eq:partial_untwisted}
\end{split}
\end{align}
More generally, if $\{i_1,\ldots,i_\ell\}\nsubseteq \{1,\ldots,n\}$,
the partially untwisted correlation functions are
given by 
the maximal subset $\{j_1,\ldots,j_{\ell'}\}\subseteq\{i_1,\ldots,i_\ell\}$
which obeys
$\{j_1,\ldots,j_{\ell'}\}\subseteq\{1,\ldots,n\}$,
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\mathcal{E}[z_{i_1},\ldots,z_{i_\ell}]
\left\{W_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}]\right\}(z_1,\ldots,z_n) \otimes_{i=1}^n dz_i 
\\
&=
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n\ge 0}
F^{(g)}[\mathsf{f}]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}
\otimes_{m=1}^{\ell'} \xi_{a_{j_m}}(z_{j_m})\,
\otimes_{k \in\{1,\ldots,n\}\setminus \{j_1,\ldots,j_{\ell'}\}}
\xi_{a_k}[\sff](z_k).
\label{eq:partial_untwisted2}
\end{split}
\end{align}



\begin{figure}[t] 
\begin{center}
\vspace{1cm}
\hspace*{-9.5cm}
 \includegraphics[bb=0 0 360 223,width=65mm]{multi_boundaries_elimination1.pdf}
 \vspace{-0cm}
\caption{\label{fig:multi_boundaries_elimination}
In the geometrical interpretation, 
the action of the twist-elimination map $\mathcal{E}(z_1,\ldots,z_n)$ on the correlation function $W_{g,n}[\sff^{\mathrm{MV}}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)$
is depicted as an elimination of the closed geodesics on the $n$  boundaries on the bordered Riemann surface
to recover the combinatorial aspects of the twisted volume in Section \ref{sect:MasurVeech}.
}
\end{center}
\end{figure}


\begin{rem}\label{rel:Picture_elimination}
In Figure \ref{fig:multi_boundaries_elimination}, the geometrical interpretation of the action of the twist-elimination map $\mathcal{E}[z_1,\ldots,z_n]$ on the correlation function $W_{g,n}[\sff^{\mathrm{MV}}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)$ is depicted.
In this picture, the correlation function is described by a capped Riemann surface where caps are glued along all boundaries in a bordered Riemann surface.
In this interpretation, the closed geodesics on the bordered boundaries and bulk in the Riemann surface
represent the Masur-Veech type twists on the bases $\xi_a[\sff^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ and
coefficients $F^{(g)}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in the multidifferential $\omega_{g,n}[\sff^{\mathrm{MV}}]$ of eq.\eqref{eq:partial_untwisted}, respectively.
In the computation of the twisted volume by the combinatorial method discussed in Section \ref{sect:MasurVeech},
we only enumerate the multicurves wrapping around the closed geodesics in the bulk of the bordered Riemann surface.
To get the twisted volume polynomial $V_{g,n}[\sff^{\mathrm{MV}}](L_1,\ldots,L_n)$ from the correlation function $W_{g,n}[\sff^{\mathrm{MV}}](z_1,\ldots,z_n)$, 
we need to eliminate the effects of twists coming from the boundaries, while keep those from the closed geodesics in the bulk.
This geometrical interpretation of the Masur-Veech type twist will be used in the physical interpretation discussed in Appendix \ref{sec:Wilson_loop}.
\end{rem}



In the following, we consider a class of twisted spectral curves with 
the coordinate functions in eq.\eqref{sp_curve} and 
twisted bidifferential \cite{Andersen_MV},
\begin{align}
B[\sfm](z_1, z_2)=\frac{dz_1 \otimes dz_2}{(z_1-z_2)^2} 
+ \frac12 \sum_{\mfm \in \IZ^*} \frac{dz_1 \otimes dz_2}{(z_1-z_2+\mfm)^2}
=\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2;z_1-z_2)\, dz_1 \otimes dz_2,
\label{bergman_twist}
\end{align}
with the Masur-Veech type twist function $\sfm$ 
in eq.\eqref{mv_twist}, where
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2d;z)&=
\frac{1}{z^{2d}} + \frac12 \sum_{\mfm \in \IZ^*} \frac{1}{(z+\mfm)^{2d}}
\\
&=
\frac{1}{z^{2d}}+
\sum_{k \ge 0}\binom{2k+2d-1}{2k}\, \zeta(2k+2d)\, z^{2k},
\label{hurwitz_def}
\end{split}
\end{align}
is the Hurwitz zeta function. 
For this twisted bidifferential $B[\sfm]$,
the recursion kernel \eqref{rec_kernel} of the CEO topological recursion yields
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
K[\sff^{\mathrm{MV}}](z,w)&=
\frac{(-1)\, dz}{\left(\sfy(w)-\sfy(-w)\right)dw}
\left(\frac{1}{z^2-w^2} + \frac12 \sum_{\mfm \in \IZ^*} \frac{1}{(z+\mfm)^2-w^2}
\right)
\\
&=
\frac{(-1)\, dz}{\left(\sfy(w)-\sfy(-w)\right)dw} 
\sum_{d\ge 0}\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2d+2;z)\, w^{2d},
\label{tw_rec_kernel}
\end{split}
\end{align}
and the twisted 1-form \eqref{eq:twisted_1-form} is
\begin{align}
\xi_a[\sfm](z)=\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2a+2;z)\, dz.
\label{twisted_1-form_sp}
\end{align}
Acting twist-elimination map $\cE$ involved with three properties of eqs.\eqref{eq:property1_elim} \eqref{eq:property2_elim} and \eqref{eq:elim_kernel} on the CEO topological recursion for the twisted spectral curve, we obtain
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\cE[z_1,z_K]\left\{W_{g,n}[\mathsf{f}^\mathrm{MV}]\right\}(z_1,z_K)
\\
&=[w^0]
\sum_{d\ge 0} \frac{w^{2d+1}}{z_1^{2d+2}\left(\sfy(w)-\sfy(-w)\right)}
\Biggl(
\sum_{m=2}^n \cE[z_m]\left\{\cW_{0,2}[\sfm]\right\}(w,z_m)
\\
&\hspace{17em}\times
\cE[z_{K\setminus \{m\}}]\left\{W_{g,n-1}[\sfm]\right\}(w,z_{K\setminus \{m\}})
\\
&\hspace{16em}
+\cE[z_K]\left\{Q_{g,n}[\sfm]\right\}(w,-w,z_K)
\Biggr),
\label{eq:top_rec_one_branch_untwisted}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $K=\{2,\ldots,n\}$, and 
$[w^0]$ implies to pick up all zeroth order terms in the expansion around $w=0$. Here 
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\cW_{0,2}[\sfm](w,z_m)
&=W_{0,2}[\sfm](w,z_m)+W_{0,2}[\sfm](-w,z_m)
\\
&=2\sum_{d\ge 0}(2d+1)\, \zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2d+2;z_m)\, w^{2d},
\label{w02_sym}
\end{split}
\end{align}
and
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
Q_{g,n}[\sfm](w,-w,z_K)&=
W_{g-1,n+1}[\sfm](w,-w,z_K)
\\
&\quad
+\sum_{\substack{h+h'=g\\ J \sqcup J'=K}}^{\mathrm{stable}}
W_{h,1+|J|}[\sfm](w,z_{J})\, W_{h',1+|J'|}[\sfm](-w,z_{J'}).
\label{ceo_rec_Q_tw}
\end{split}
\end{align}
We refer to the recursion \eqref{eq:top_rec_one_branch_untwisted} 
as the \emph{partially twist-eliminated CEO topological recursion}.

In the rest of this section, we provide a direct proof of the following claim.

\begin{thm}[Laplace transform of the twisted volume polynomial \cite{Andersen_GR,Andersen_MV}]\label{thm:Laplace_dual_GR}
For the $(2,p)$ minimal string and the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring, 
the twisted correlation function $W_{g,n}[\sfm](z_1,\ldots,z_n)$ with the action of the twist-elimination map $\mathcal{E}$ 
agrees with the Laplace transform $\mathcal{L}$ 
of the twisted volume polynomial $V_{g,n}[\sfm](L_1,\ldots,L_n)$:
\begin{align}
\mathcal{L}\left\{V_{g,n}[\sfm]\right\}(z_1,\ldots,z_n)=
\cE[z_1,\ldots,z_n]\left\{W_{g,n}[\sfm]\right\}(z_1,\ldots,z_n),
\label{eq:Laplace_dual_GR}
\end{align}
where the operator $\mathcal{L}$ is defined by eq.\eqref{eq:Laplace}.
\end{thm}





\subsubsection{The Laplace dual relation for $(2,p)$ minimal string}\label{sec:Laplace_bosonic}

We will show that the Laplace dual relation \eqref{eq:Laplace_dual_GR} holds for the $(2,p)$ minimal string manifestly.%
\footnote{This relation is derived formally in the general set-up in \cite{Andersen_MV}.
In this article, we give direct proofs specialized for the physical 2D gravity models. 
}
Accordingly, by the specializations $p=\infty$ and $1$,
we also find that the Laplace dual relation holds for the  Weil-Petersson volumes and the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes, respectively.


\begin{prop}\label{prop:Laplace_dual_untwisted}
For the $(2,p)$ minimal string, the Laplace transform of
the Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion \eqref{eq:Mirzakhani's} 
with the Masur-Veech type twist,
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&\label{eq:Laplace_dual_untwisted}
\int_{\IR_+^n}
\Biggl[
\sum_{m=2}^n \int_{\IR_+} \left(R(L_1,L_m,x) + L_1 \sfm(x)\right)
xV_{g,n-1}[\sfm](x,L_{K\setminus \{m\}})\, dx
\\
&\qquad
+\frac{1}{2}\int_{\IR_+^2}
\left(D(L_1,x,y)+R(L_1,x,y)\, \sfm(y) + R(L_1,y,x)\, \sfm(x) + 
L_1 \sfm(x)\, \sfm(y)\right)
\\
&\hspace{14em}
\times xyP_{g,n}[\sfm](x,y,L_K)\, dxdy
\Biggr]
\e^{-z_1L_1}\, dL_1
\prod_{i=2}^n \e^{-z_iL_i}\, L_idL_i,
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $P_{g,n}[\sfm](x,y,L_K)$ is given by eq.\eqref{geo_rec_p} 
for the twisted volume polynomials, 
agrees with the partially twist-eliminated CEO topological recursion \eqref{eq:top_rec_one_branch_untwisted} for $2g-2+n > 1$.
\end{prop}

To prove this proposition, 
we prepare some key integration formulae involving the kernel function $H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,y)$ in eq.\eqref{eq:H_minimal} 
for the $(2,p)$ minimal string. (See eqs.(2.2) and (2.3) in \cite{MulSaf} for analogous formulae of the Mirzakhani's recursion for the Weil-Petersson volumes.)
For $k\in\mathbb{Z}_{\ge 0}$, one finds
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
h_{2k+1}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(t):=&\,
\int_{\IR_+} \frac{x^{2k+1}}{(2k+1)!}\, H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,t)\, dx
\\
=&\,
\frac{t^{2k+2}}{(2k+2)!}
-2\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}
(-1)^{j}\cos\left(\frac{\pi}{p}j\right)
\sum_{\ell=0}^{k}u_j^{2\ell-2k-2}\frac{t^{2\ell}}{(2\ell)!}
\\
=&\,
\sum_{\ell=0}^{k+1}s_{\ell}\, \frac{t^{2k+2-2\ell}}{(2k+2-2\ell)!},
\label{eq:formula1}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $u_j=(p/2\pi)\sin(j\pi/p)$ in eq.\eqref{eq:uj_bosonic}, and
\begin{align}
\int_{\IR_+^2}\frac{x^{2a+1}y^{2b+1}}{(2a+1)!(2b+1)!}\, H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x+y,t)\, dxdy=h_{2a+2b+3}^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(t).
\label{eq:formula2}
\end{align}
The coefficients $s_{\ell}$'s in eq.\eqref{eq:formula1} agree with 
those in the following expansion for $1/\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)$
of the $(2,p)$ minimal string spectral curve:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\frac{1}{\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(z)}&=
(-1)^{\frac{p-1}{2}}\frac{2\pi}{T_p\left(\frac{2\pi}{p}z\right)}
=\frac{1}{z}+\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}
(-1)^j\cos\left(\frac{\pi}{p}j\right)\left(
\frac{1}{z-u_j}+\frac{1}{z+u_j}
\right)
\\
&=\sum_{\ell \ge 0}s_\ell\, z^{2\ell-1}.
\label{eq:1/y}
\end{split}
\end{align}
In addition, we will use an integration formula involving the Masur-Veech type twist function,
\begin{align}
\int_{\IR_+}\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(x)\, x^{2k+1}\, dx
=(2k+1)!\, \zeta(2k+2).
\label{eq:twist_zeta}
\end{align}


\begin{lem}\label{lem:Laplace_B-term}
In eq.\eqref{eq:Laplace_dual_untwisted}, 
the $x^{2k+1}$ term in $V_{g,n-1}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](x,L_{K\setminus\{m\}})$ obeys
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\int_{\IR_+^3}
\left(R(L_1,L_m,x)+L_1\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(x)\right)x^{2k+1}\,
\mathrm{e}^{-z_1L_1-z_mL_m}\, dx\, dL_1\, L_mdL_m
\\
&
=\frac{1}{2}[w^0]\sum_{d\ge 0} \frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}\frac{w^{2d+1}}{\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(w)}\,
\mathcal{E}[z_m]\left\{\cW_{0,2}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]\right\}(w,z_m)\,
\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2k+2;w)\, (2k+1)!.
\label{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic}
\end{split}
\end{align}
\end{lem}
\begin{proof}
We perform the integrations on the left hand side of eq.\eqref{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic} using eqs.\eqref{eq:DR_H_bosonic}, \eqref{eq:formula1} and \eqref{eq:twist_zeta}:
\begin{align}
\label{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic_LHS}
&
\int_{\IR_+^3}
\left[
\frac12 \int_{0}^{L_1}
\left(H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,t+L_m)+H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,t-L_m)\right)dt 
+ L_1 \sfm(x)\right]
x^{2k+1}\,
\\
&\qquad\times
\mathrm{e}^{-z_1L_1-z_mL_m}\, dx\, dL_1\, L_mdL_m 
\nonumber\\
&=(2k+1)!\left(\sum_{\ell=0}^{k+1}\sum_{d=0}^{k+1-\ell}s_{\ell}
\cdot(2k+3-2\ell-2d) \frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}\frac{1}{z_m^{2k+4-2\ell-2d}}
+\frac{1}{z_1^2}\frac{1}{z_m^2}\, \zeta(2k+2)\right),
\nonumber
\end{align}
where we also used 
a formula of the Laplace transform:
\begin{align}
\int_{\IR_+} L^{n}\, \mathrm{e}^{-zL}\, dL=\frac{n!}{z^{n+1}}.
\label{eq:Laplace_basic}
\end{align}
On the other hand, the right hand side of eq.\eqref{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic} 
is rewritten, by eq.\eqref{w02_sym}, as
\begin{align}
\frac{1}{2}[w^0]\sum_{d\ge 0}\frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}\frac{w^{2d+1}}{\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(w)}
\left(2\sum_{d'\ge 0}(2d'+1)\frac{w^{2d'}}{z_m^{2d'+2}}\right)
\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2k+2;w)\, (2k+1)!.
\label{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic_RHS}
\end{align}
Adopting the formula \eqref{hurwitz_def} for $\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2k+2;w)$ 
and the expansion \eqref{eq:1/y} for $1/\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(w)$ to this expression,
we find the agreement between eqs.\eqref{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic_LHS} and \eqref{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic_RHS}.
\end{proof}


\begin{lem}\label{lem:Laplace_C-term}
In eq.\eqref{eq:Laplace_dual_untwisted}, 
the $x^{2a+1}y^{2b+1}$ term in $P_{g,n}[\sfm](x,y,L_K)$ obeys
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\frac{1}{2}\int_{\IR_+^3}
\left(D(L_1,x,y)+R(L_1,x,y)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(y)
+R(L_1,y,x)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(x)
+L_1\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(x)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(y)\right)
\\
&\qquad\times
x^{2a+1}y^{2b+1}\, \e^{-z_1L_1}\, dxdydL_1
\\
&
=\frac{1}{2}[w^0]
\sum_{d\ge 0}\frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}
\frac{w^{2d+1}}{\sfy^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(w)}
\left(\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2a+2;w)\, (2a+1)!\right)
\left(\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2b+2;w)\, (2b+1)!\right).
\label{eq:twist_C-term_bosonic}
\end{split}
\end{align}
\end{lem}
\begin{proof}
We perform the integrations for each term on the left hand side of eq.\eqref{eq:twist_C-term_bosonic} using eqs.\eqref{eq:DR_H_bosonic}, 
\eqref{eq:formula1}, \eqref{eq:formula2} and \eqref{eq:twist_zeta}.
The term involving $D(L_1,x,y)$ yields:
\begin{align}
\label{eq:Laplace_C-term_1}
&
\frac{1}{2}\int_{\IR_+^3}
\left(\int_0^{L_1} H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x+y,t)\, dt\right)
x^{2a+1}y^{2b+1}\, \e^{-z_1L_1}\, dxdydL_1
\\
&=\frac{1}{2}(2a+1)!(2b+1)!
\sum_{\ell=0}^{a+b+2} \frac{s_{\ell}}{z_1^{2a+2b-2\ell+4}}.
\nonumber
\end{align}
The term involving $R(L_1,x,y)\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(y)$ yields:
\begin{align}
\label{eq:Laplace_C-term_2}
&
\frac{1}{4}\int_{\IR_+^3}
\left(\int_0^{L_1}\left(H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,t+y)+H^{\mathrm{M}(p)}(x,t-y)\right)dt\right) 
x^{2a+1}y^{2b+1}\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(y)\, \e^{-z_1L_1}\, dxdydL_1
\\
&=\frac{1}{2}(2a+1)!
\sum_{\ell=0}^{a+1}\sum_{d=0}^{a+1-\ell}s_{\ell}\, \frac{(2a+2b+3-2\ell-2d)!}{(2a+2-2\ell-2d)!}\,
\zeta(2a+2b+4-2\ell-2d)\, \frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}},
\nonumber
\end{align}
and we find the term involving $R(L_1,y,x)\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(x)$ by replacing the role of parameters $a$ and $b$ in eq.\eqref{eq:Laplace_C-term_2}:
\begin{align}
\label{eq:Laplace_C-term_3}
\frac{1}{2}(2b+1)!
\sum_{\ell=0}^{b+1}\sum_{d=0}^{b+1-\ell}s_{\ell}\, \frac{(2a+2b+3-2\ell-2d)!}{(2b+2-2\ell-2d)!}\,
\zeta(2a+2b+4-2\ell-2d)\, \frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}.
\end{align}
Finally the term involving $\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(x)\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(y)$ yields:
\begin{align}
\label{eq:Laplace_C-term_4}
\frac{1}{2z_1^2}\, (2a+1)!\, (2b+1)!\, \zeta(2a+2)\, \zeta(2b+2). 
\end{align}
On the other hand, 
adopting eqs.\eqref{hurwitz_def} and \eqref{eq:1/y} on the right hand side of eq.\eqref{eq:twist_C-term_bosonic}, 
we correctly recover the sum of four terms \eqref{eq:Laplace_C-term_1} -- \eqref{eq:Laplace_C-term_4}.
\end{proof}

Combining the claims in Lemmas \ref{lem:Laplace_B-term} and \ref{lem:Laplace_C-term} as well as 
the expansions \eqref{eq:expansion_volume} and \eqref{eq:twisted_multidifferential} with \eqref{twisted_1-form_sp}, 
we find the claim of Proposition \ref{prop:Laplace_dual_untwisted}.



\subsubsection{The Laplace dual relation for $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring}\label{sec:Laplace_super}

We will show that the Laplace dual relation \eqref{eq:Laplace_dual_GR} holds for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring.
Accordingly, by the specializations $p=\infty$ and $1$,
we also find that the Laplace dual relation holds for the super Weil-Petersson volumes and the supersymmetric analogue of the Kontsevich-Witten symplectic volumes, respectively.


\begin{prop}\label{prop:Laplace_dual_untwisted_super}
For the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring, the Laplace transform of
the Mirzakhani type ABO topological recursion \eqref{eq:Mirzakhani's}
with the Masur-Veech type twist,
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&\label{eq:Laplace_dual_untwisted_super}
\int_{\IR_+^n}
\Biggl[
\sum_{m=2}^n \int_{\IR_+} R(L_1,L_m,x)\, 
xV_{g,n-1}[\sfm](x,L_{K\setminus \{m\}})\, dx
\\
&\qquad
+\frac{1}{2}\int_{\IR_+^2}
\left(D(L_1,x,y)+R(L_1,x,y)\, \sfm(y) + R(L_1,y,x)\, \sfm(x)\right)
\\
&\hspace{6em}
\times xyP_{g,n}[\sfm](x,y,L_K)\, dxdy
\Biggr]
\e^{-z_1L_1}\, dL_1
\prod_{i=2}^n \e^{-z_iL_i}\, L_idL_i,
\end{split}
\end{align}
agrees with the partially twist-eliminated CEO topological recursion \eqref{eq:top_rec_one_branch_untwisted} for $2g-2+n > 1$.
\end{prop}


To prove Proposition \ref{prop:Laplace_dual_untwisted_super}, we use 
an integration formula
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
h_{2k+1}^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(t):=&\,
\int_{\IR_+} \frac{x^{2k+1}}{(2k+1)!}\, H^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(x,t)\, dx
\\
=&\,
\frac{t^{2k+1}\, \delta_{p,1}}{(2k+1)!}
-\frac{1}{\pi}\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}
(-1)^{j}\cos^2\left(\frac{\pi}{p}\left(j-\frac{1}{2}\right)\right)
\sum_{\ell=0}^{k}(u'_j)^{2\ell-2k-1}\frac{t^{2\ell+1}}{(2\ell+1)!}
\\
=&\,
\sum_{\ell=0}^{k} s'_{\ell}\, \frac{t^{2k+1-2\ell}}{(2k+1-2\ell)!},
\label{eq:formula1_super}
\end{split}
\end{align}
involving the kernel function $H^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(x,y)$ in eq.\eqref{eq:H_super_minimal} for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring,
where $u_j'=(p/2\pi)\sin((j-1/2)\pi/p)$ in eq.\eqref{eq:uj_super}.
(See Section 5.4 of \cite{Norbury:2020vyi} for an analogous formula of the Stanford-Witten's recursion for the super Weil-Petersson volumes.)
The following expansion for the $(2,2p-2)$ minimal superstring spectral curve 
also gives the coefficients $s'_{\ell}$'s in eq.\eqref{eq:formula1_super}:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\frac{1}{\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z)}&=
(-1)^{\frac{p-1}{2}}\frac{z}{U_{p-1}\left(\frac{2\pi}{p}z\right)}
\\
&=z\, \delta_{p,1}+\frac{z}{2\pi}\sum_{j=1}^{(p-1)/2}
(-1)^j \cos^2\left(\frac{\pi}{p}\left(j-\frac{1}{2}\right)\right)\left(
\frac{1}{z-u'_j}-\frac{1}{z+u'_j}
\right)
\\
&=\sum_{\ell \ge 0}s'_{\ell}\, z^{2\ell+1}.
\label{eq:1/y_super}
\end{split}
\end{align}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:Laplace_B-term_super}
In eq.\eqref{eq:Laplace_dual_untwisted_super}, 
the $x^{2k+1}$ term in $V_{g,n-1}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}](x,L_{K \setminus\{m\}})$ obeys
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\int_{\IR_+^3} R(L_1,L_m,x)\, x^{2k+1}\, \e^{-z_1L_1-z_mL_m}\, 
dx\, dL_1\, L_mdL_m
\\
&
=\frac{1}{2}[w^0]\sum_{d\ge 0}\frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}
\frac{w^{2d+1}}{\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(w)}\,
\mathcal{\cE}[z_m]\left\{\cW_{0,2}[\mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}]\right\}(w,z_m)\,
\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2k+2;w)\, (2k+1)!.
\label{eq:twist_B-term_super}
\end{split}
\end{align}
\end{lem}
\begin{proof}
The equation \eqref{eq:twist_B-term_super} is verified in the parallel way as eq.\eqref{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic}.
We rewrite the left hand side of eq.\eqref{eq:twist_B-term_super} 
by eqs.\eqref{eq:DR_H_super}, \eqref{eq:Laplace_basic}, and \eqref{eq:formula1_super}:
\begin{align}
&
\frac12\int_{\IR_+^3}
\left(H^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(x,L_1+L_m)+H^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(x,L_1-L_m)\right)
x^{2k+1}\, \e^{-z_1L_1-z_mL_m}\, 
dx\, dL_1\, L_mdL_m
\label{eq:twist_B-term_super_LHS}
\\
&=(2k+1)!\sum_{\ell=0}^{k}\sum_{d=0}^{k-\ell}s'_{\ell}\cdot(2k-2\ell-2d+1)
\frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}\frac{1}{z_m^{2k-2\ell-2d+2}}.
\nonumber 
\end{align}
The right hand side of eq.\eqref{eq:twist_B-term_super} is rewritten in the same form \eqref{eq:twist_B-term_bosonic_RHS} as the $(2,p)$ minimal string.
By the formula \eqref{hurwitz_def} for $\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2k+2;w)$ 
and the expansion \eqref{eq:1/y_super} for $1/\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(z)$, 
the claim follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:Laplace_C-term_super}
In eq.\eqref{eq:Laplace_dual_untwisted_super}, 
the $x^{2a+1}y^{2b+1}$ term in $P_{g,n}[\sfm](x,y,L_K)$ obeys
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
&
\frac{1}{2}\int_{\IR_+^3}
\left(D(L_1,x,y)+R(L_1,x,y)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(y)
+R(L_1,y,x)\, \mathsf{f}^{\mathrm{MV}}(x)\right)
x^{2a+1}y^{2b+1}\, \e^{-z_1L_1}\, dxdydL_1
\\
&
=\frac{1}{2}[w^0]
\sum_{d\ge 0}\frac{1}{z_1^{2d+2}}
\frac{w^{2d+1}}{\sfy^{\mathrm{SM}(p)}(w)}
\left(\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2a+2;w)\, (2a+1)!\right)
\left(\zeta_{\mathrm{H}}(2b+2;w)\, (2b+1)!\right).
\label{eq:twist_C-term_super}
\end{split}
\end{align}
\end{lem}
\begin{proof}
The equation \eqref{eq:twist_C-term_super} is verified in the parallel way as eq.\eqref{eq:twist_C-term_bosonic}.
\end{proof}

Combining the claims in Lemmas \ref{lem:Laplace_B-term_super} and \ref{lem:Laplace_C-term_super}, we find the claim of Proposition \ref{prop:Laplace_dual_untwisted_super}.





%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Virasoro constraints}\label{sec:virasoro_constraint}

In this section, we first overview an algebraic formulation, called the quantum Airy structures \cite{Kontsevich:2017vdc,Andersen:2017vyk}, 
of the ABO topological recursion and the CEO topological recursion. 
In particular, we will see the equivalence between 
the quantum Airy structures and the Virasoro constraints
for the physical 2D gravity models in Table \ref{tab:spectral_curve}. 
We then discuss explicit computation of the volume coefficients 
$F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ as well as the twisted volume coefficients 
$F^{(g)}[\sfm]_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ using 
the cut-and-join equations in \cite{Alexandrov:2010bn,Alexandrov:2016kjl} 
derived from the Virasoro constraints and homogeneity conditions, 
and a group action in \cite{Andersen:2017vyk} which is associated with the twist action.



\subsection{Formulation}\label{sec:def_vir}

Consider the generating function of the volume coefficients 
$F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}$ in eq.\eqref{gr_exp} of the ABO topological recursion 
or eq.\eqref{laplace_exp} of the CEO topological recursion for $2g-2+n > 0$:
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
Z(\hbar; \textbf{t})&=\e^{F(\hbar; \textbf{t})},
\\
F(\hbar; \textbf{t})
&=
\sum_{g \ge 0} \hbar^{2g-2} F_{g}(\textbf{t})
=
\sum_{g \ge 0, n\ge 1} \hbar^{2g-2} 
\sum_{a_1,\ldots,a_n \ge 0} F^{(g)}_{a_1,\ldots,a_n}\,
\frac{t_{a_1}\cdots t_{a_n}}{n!}.
\label{gen_fn}
\end{split}
\end{align}
Here $\textbf{t}=\{t_0, t_1, t_2, \ldots \}$ is the set of variables $t_a$
which are related to the length variables $L_i$ in eq.\eqref{gr_exp}
and the spectral curve variables $z_i$ in eq.\eqref{laplace_exp} by
\begin{align}
\frac{t_{a_1}\cdots t_{a_n}}{n!}
\ \ \longleftrightarrow\ \
\frac{L_1^{2a_1}}{(2a_1+1)!} \cdots \frac{L_n^{2a_n}}{(2a_n+1)!}
\ \ \longleftrightarrow\ \
\frac{1}{z_1^{2a_1+2}} \cdots \frac{1}{z_n^{2a_n+2}}.
\label{variables_rel}
\end{align}
In this set of variables, the recursion \eqref{geom_rec_coeff} leads to
\begin{align}
\begin{split}
\partial_{k} F(\hbar; \textbf{t})&=
\sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfB^{k}_{a, b}\, t_a \partial_b F(\hbar; \textbf{t})
+ \frac{\hbar^2}{2} \sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfC^{k}_{a, b}
\left(\partial_a \partial_b F(\hbar; \textbf{t}) 
+ \partial_a F(\hbar; \textbf{t})\, \partial_b F(\hbar; \textbf{t}) \right)
\\
&\quad
+ \frac{1}{2\hbar^2} \sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfA^{k}_{a, b}\, t_a t_b
+ \sfD^{k},
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $\partial_a = \partial/\partial t_a$, 
and the following proposition is obtained.


\begin{prop}[\cite{Andersen:2017vyk}]\label{prop:viraroso_const}
The generating function \eqref{gen_fn} satisfies constraint equations,
\begin{align}
\widehat{L}_k\, Z(\hbar; \textbf{t})=0,\qquad
k \ge -1,
\label{airy_constraint}
\end{align}
where
\begin{align}
\widehat{L}_k=
-\frac12 \partial_{k+1}
+ \frac{1}{4\hbar^2} \sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfA^{k+1}_{a, b}\, t_a t_b
+ \frac12 \sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfB^{k+1}_{a, b}\, t_a \partial_b
+ \frac{\hbar^2}{4} \sum_{a, b \ge 0} \sfC^{k+1}_{a, b}\, \partial_a \partial_b
+ \frac12 \sfD^{k+1}.
\label{airy_gen}
\end{align}
\end{prop}


When the differential operators $\widehat{L}_k$ satisfy
\begin{align}
\big[\widehat{L}_k, \widehat{L}_{\ell} \big]
= \sum_{a \ge -1} f^{a}_{k,\ell}\, \widehat{L}_{a},
\qquad
k, \ell \ge -1,
\label{q_airy_rel}
\end{align}
where $f^{a}_{k,\ell}$ are scalars, the operators $\widehat{L}_k$ define
